This is a tried and true recipe and you will agree that it is the best recipe out there!\nThis is my most popular recipe for a good reason! If you love alfredo as much as I do try this Creamy Garlic Shrimp Alfredo Pasta , Instant Pot Chicken Alfredo Pasta or Asiago Garlic Alfredo Pasta .\u00a0\nAlfredo Sauce\nI just had to post my favorite alfredo recipe that I have created here on the blog.\nThere are a few secret ingredients that set it apart from all of the rest.\nIf there is one thing I can always count on my family to eat it is my homemade alfredo sauce over pasta.\nWe recently had some company over for\u00a0dinner and I made these Chicken Bacon Garlic Alfredo Roll Ups and they always are a huge hit!\nThis alfredo sauce is thick and creamy and the flavor is out of the world.\nIt is restaurant quality that you can make right at home!\nWhat is Alfredo Sauce\nClassic Alfredo Sauce is a simple but elegant creamy, white sauce that is commonly known to lay over pasta noodles.\nIt is made from butter, a type of cream and parmesan cheese.\nAdding seasonings and cream cheese for a thickener I like to blend a rich, creamy sauce together that is simple and irresistible.\nThe end result of this mixture is satisfying to say the least!\nWhat you need to make alfredo sauce\nSimple ingredients for an elegant sauce that is a classic dish loved by all.\nAlfredo Sauce just has a smooth, creamy texture that melts in your mouth.\nThe best results comes from the ingredients. Using the freshest ingredients is key!\nFresh parmesan cheese grated off the block is one of those key ingredients.\nThis will create a smooth textured sauce rather than a grainy one.\nEach of these ingredients melt and blend together so well creating a masterpiece!\nButter: either unsalted or salted work for this alfredo sauce recipe.\nHeavy whipping cream:\u00a0 for a richer and creamy flavor heavy whipping cream is preferred over whipping cream.\nCream cheese: this adds a nice thick consistency to your alfredo sauce.\nMinced garlic: for best flavoring use fresh garlic and mince it the best you can.\nGarlic powder: adds to the rich and garlic flavoring.\nItalian seasoning: brings on an Italian fill and blends all the seasonings together.\nSalt and pepper: just to taste!\nGrated parmesan cheese: using real parmesan cheese is best. Powdered cheese will create a grainy texture and does not melt through when heated.\nHow to make Alfredo sauce\nCreating this master piece does take a little bit of time. We all know that it is worth it!\nWe love Alfredo sauce and it is a quick and easy sauce that can be made in minutes with these simple ingredients.\nEnjoy alfredo sauce right when you need it!\nWhisk dairy ingredients together: In a medium saucepan add butter, heavy whipping cream, and cream cheese. Cook over medium heat and whisk until melted.\nAdd and whisk seasonings:\u00a0 Add the minced garlic, garlic powder, italian seasoning, salt and pepper. Continue to whisk until smooth.\nStir in cheese:\u00a0 Add the grated parmesan cheese.\nThicken your sauce:\u00a0 Bring to a simmer and continue to cook for about 3-5 minutes or until it starts to thicken.\nToss with pasta:\u00a0 Toss it with your favorite pasta!\nIs Alfredo Sauce keto?\nYes! This is totally keto! I left out the flour and that makes this keto.\nCrazy, I know! But such good news!\nIf you are following a low carb diet this can be a great recipe to enjoy while cutting back on other favorite meals.\nEven though it is keto and considered a low carb recipe, it is still full on creamy, thick and rich alfredo sauce.\nIt will be like dessert in your mouth!\nThis easy to make Alfredo Sauce recipe will have you saying MMMMM and AWW, with every bite.\nFAQ\u2019s for making Alfredo Sauce\nThis alfredo sauce has delicious garlic flavor and Italian seasonings.\nI like to add cream cheese to my alfredo for that extra creamy flavor and texture.\nThis alfredo sauce always gets raved about whenever I make it!\nHow to make\u00a0Alfredo Sauce with milk instead cream?\nAdding milk is always an option. This will be a lighter and less thick consistency but can work. Half and half is also another option instead of heavy whipping cream. To thicken it up a little more adding 1 to 2 teaspoons of flour to thicken.\nHow to make\u00a0Alfredo\u00a0Sauce thicker?\nWhen adding cream cheese, slowly cut chunks of cream cheese as you are stirring. This helps create a thicker and creamier sauce. You can also use a roux by using an equal amount of butter to flour, about 1 teaspoon.\nIs\u00a0Alfredo Sauce gluten free?\nThis recipe is considered gluten free! It still has a great taste and all the fresh ingredients to make this just the way you like it with no substitutions.\nIs Alfredo Sauce cheese?\nThis is a cheese based sauce that is rich in flavor. It does not harden like a cheese though.\nDoes Alfredo\u00a0sauce have dairy?\nThere are substitutions to make this dairy free but I do not recommend it if you are looking for the authentic taste of Alfredo Sauce. Having dairy in this Alfredo Sauce recipe makes this rich, creamy and smooth when simmering.\nIs Alfredo Sauce good with ground beef?\u00a0\nIt can be done, but not recommended. Alfredo sauce goes best with a chicken, fish or pasta.\nHow Many Cups Does this Yield?\nWhen you are done making your Alfredo Sauce you will be able to fill a tall canning jar. This is about 14 to 16 ounces (1 pound) of pasta or 2 cups of sauce. We like to reserve a little alfredo sauce on the side for dipping.\u00a0\nTips for making Alfredo Sauce\nI think this sauce is even better than any restaurant that I have been to and the best part is that you can make it yourself!\nIt is thick, creamy, and rich and the perfect sauce on top of your favorite pasta.\nI know that you will quickly agree that this is the BEST!\nThis will be a recipe that you make again and again, just like I do!\nSlowly add in your heavy whipping cream and cream cheese. This will enhance your flavors as well as thicken evenly throughout.\nAvoid separating your Alfredo Sauce when mixing it by whisking it together rather than stirring with a spatula.\nParmesan cheese is the key ingredient for making this Alfredo Sauce thick and creamy. I recommend using a fresh parmesan cheese that you grate yourself or similar. Try to avoid using the powder or grated grated parmesan cheese in a tall can.\nThe most important rule is not overheating your Alfredo Sauce. Slowly add ingredients on a low and for a short period of time. Melted cheese will break and separate once it gets too hot leaving your cheese clumpy.\nWhen simmering, a shorter amount of time is best. Around 1 minute, whisking it well.\nDo not boil or overheat. Boiling will separate and ruin the alfredo sauce.\nIf you are worried about overheating, add your parmesan with the heat off. This will also precent clumping and separating the alfredo sauce.\nVariations of alfredo sauce\nThere are many variations that can be done with Alfredo Sauce recipe.\nAdding thickeners or making it more creamy and watery are great ways to adjust this Alfredo Sauce.\nSubstituting any dairy or cheese can have major changes to this alfredo sauce recipe though.\nFor best results, enjoy my delicious Alfredo Sauce recipe that is definitely a tried and true recipe that is pure perfection!\nHalf and half or milk is great to substitute the heavy whipping cream.\nGrilled chicken, shredding rotisserie chicken or shrimp goes well with pasta.\nAdd in more spices and seasonings like red pepper flakes or paprika for a sweeter and spicier Alfredo Sauce like this\u00a0 One Pot Cajun Chicken Alfredo Pasta .\nUse half Romano cheese or asiago cheese instead of parmesan cheese.\nMaking your own fresh pasta instead of dry pasta tastes even more amazing.\nWays to use Alfredo Sauce\nThis alfredo sauce recipe comes together pretty easily and you will never go back to the jarred alfredo sauce again! \u00a0\nIt is awesome on top of just about any pasta but is also delicious used as a dip or even spread on pizza .\nYou can\u2019t go wrong where you add your Alfredo Sauce to!\nPasta : Any pasta is great with Alfredo Sauce. The thicker and larger is best to soak up the rich, thick and creamy sauce.\nPizza: \u00a0Alfredo pizza is one of our favorites. We love the fresh and lighter taste this sauce has to offer. This Chicken Alfredo Pizza is a great use of Alfredo Sauce recipe. Making my Quick and Easy Dough \u00a0for the crust is a great combination too.\nDipping: \u00a0We love to dip breadsticks or Miracle No Knead Bread . It is always so delicious and almost addicting it is so good!\nCasserole: \u00a0I have several casserole dishes that work so well with this alfredo sauce. It is easy to make and add to a simple casserole. Try this Pesto Alfredo Chicken Casserole for your next main meal!\nWhat to make with Alfredo Sauce\nAlfredo sauce is a family favorite over here.\nI know that I can make so many delicious recipes with this Alfredo Sauce.\nSimple and basic recipes to a little more complex, this Alfredo Sauce recipe just does the trick!\nMake this a complete meal with a few vegetables, garlic bread and a side salad.\nGrilled Asparagus\nParmesan Roasted Vegetables\u00a0\nThree Cheese Garlic Pull Apart Bread\nChilled Cucumber Tomato Salad\nSkillet Potatoes with Peppers\nHow to store alfredo sauce\nTo make the perfect blend of Alfredo Sauce you will want to watch your cooking temperature and stirring well.\nThis will make the perfect alfredo sauce and reheating just a breeze.\nAlfredo Sauce is a favorite in our home and I know that it does not last long, even if I double it!\nEnjoy your Alfredo Sauce again and again when storing it properly.\nHow long does Alfredo sauce last in the fridge: I like to pour my Alfredo Sauce in a jar and sealed in the refrigerator. For best results and continued flavoring it will last in the fridge for about 5 days.\nCan you freeze Alfredo\u00a0Sauce: Unfortunately this Alfredo Sauce does not freeze well. Because of the freshness of it, it will separate when freezing.\nHow to heat up Alfredo sauce: Slowly, is the key! Slow, low temperatures and stirring often. If it starts to separate, slowly stir it back together over low heat on the stove top. It is best not to microwave this sauce. It becomes more oily and separates just as easily, if not more. Once reheated, do not reheat again.\nMore delicious recipes using alfredo sauce\nAlfredo Pesto Tortellini with Sausage\u00a0\nChicken Broccoli Garlic Alfredo Shells\nBacon Chicken Alfredo Pizza\nSkinny Fettuccini Garlic Alfredo\u00a0\nThree Cheese Chicken Broccoli Alfredo\u00a0\nThe Best Homemade Alfredo Sauce Ever!\n4.9 from 473 votes\nPrep Time\n10\nminutes\nCook Time\n5\nminutes\nTotal Time\n15\nminutes\nAuthor\nAlyssa Rivers\nServings\n10\nservings\nPrint\nReview\nAlfredo\u00a0Sauce is the most creamy and delicious homemade alfredo sauce that you will ever make! \u00a0 This is a tried and true recipe and you will agree that it is the best recipe out there!\nCourse\nDinner, Main Course\nCuisine\nItalian\nIngredients\n\u00bd\ncup\nbutter\n1\npint\nheavy whipping cream\n2 cups\n4\nounces\ncream cheese\n\u00bd\nteaspoon\nminced garlic\n1\nteaspoon\ngarlic powder\n1\nteaspoon\nitalian seasoning\n\u00bc\nteaspoon\nsalt\n\u00bc\nteaspoon\npepper\n1\ncup\ngrated parmesan cheese\nInstructions\nIn a medium saucepan add butter, heavy whipping cream, and cream cheese. Cook over medium heat and whisk until melted. \u00a0\nAdd the minced garlic, garlic powder, italian seasoning, salt and pepper. Continue to whisk until smooth. Add the grated parmesan cheese.\nBring to a simmer and continue to cook for about 3-5 minutes or until it starts to thicken. Toss it with your favorite pasta!\nRecipe Video\nhttps://therecipecritic.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/THE20BEST20HOMEMADE20ALFREDO20SAUCE20RECIPE20EVER21.mp4\nRecipe Notes\nUpdated on October 24, 2019\nOriginal Post on February 18, 2016\nNutrition Facts\nThe Best Homemade Alfredo Sauce Ever!\nAmount Per Serving\nCalories 329\nCalories from Fat 297\n% Daily Value*\nFat 33g 51%\nSaturated Fat 21g 105%\nCholesterol 111mg 37%\nSodium 347mg 14%\nPotassium 67mg 2%\nCarbohydrates 3g 1%\nFiber 1g 4%\nSugar 1g 1%\nProtein 6g 12%\nVitamin A 1218IU 24%\nVitamin C 1mg 1%\nCalcium 159mg 16%\nIron 1mg 6%\n* Percent Daily Values are based on a 2000 calorie diet.\n\u00a0\nSave\nSave\nSave\nShare The Post!\nShare on Facebook 0 Pin on Pinterest 0 Share via Email 0\nGet free recipes to your inbox!\nPlease enable JavaScript in your browser to complete this form.\nYour First Name *\nYour Email Address *\nMessage\nSubmit\nAlyssa Rivers\nI am Alyssa and the blogger behind The Recipe Critic. "title": ["Alfredo alla Scrofa - Wikipedia"], "url": ["https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_alla_Scrofa"], "content": ["Alfredo alla Scrofa - Wikipedia\nAlfredo alla Scrofa\nFrom Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\nJump to navigation\nJump to search\nAlfredo alla Scrofa Restaurant information Established 1914 ; 106\u00a0years ago \u00a0( 1914 ) Food type Italian cuisine Street address Via della Scrofa, 104/a, 00186 City Rome Country Italy Website www .alfredoallascrofa .com\nAlfredo alla Scrofa is an Italian restaurant in Rome , Italy . [1] It has been operating since 1914 and is known as the birthplace of Fettuccine Alfredo . [2]\nHistory [ edit ]\nAlfredo Di Lelio, founder of Alfredo alla Scrofa, claims to be the creator of Fettuccine Alfredo . [2] According to family accounts, in 1892 Alfredo Di Lelio began to work in a restaurant that was located in piazza Rosa and run by his mother Angelina. Di Lelio invented \"fettuccine al triplo burro\" [3] (later named \"fettuccine all'Alfredo\" or \"fettuccine Alfredo\") in 1907 or 1908, while running an oil and wine shop, in an effort to entice his wife, Ines, to eat after giving birth to their first child Armando. Alfredo added extra butter or \"triplo burro\u201d to the fettuccine when mixing it together for her. [4] [5] [6]\nIn 1914, Di Lelio converted the oil and wine shop into the restaurant, then called \"Alfredo\", on the via della Scrofa in central Rome. [7] In 1943, Di Lelio sold the restaurant to the family of the current owners. In 1950 Alfredo Di Lelio decided to reopen with his son Armando his restaurant in Piazza Augusto Imperatore n.30 \"Il Vero Alfredo\" (\u201cAlfredo di Roma\u201d), that is always operational, managed by Alfredo Di Lelio's family.\nReferences [ edit ]\n^\nLaurie Bogart Morrow (9 October 2012). Retrieved 12 December 2018 .\nExternal links [ edit ]\nOfficial website (in Italian and English)\nRetrieved from \" https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alfredo_alla_Scrofa&oldid=934730715 \"\nCategories :\nRestaurants in Rome\nRestaurants established in 1914\n1914 establishments in Italy\nHidden categories:\nCS1 Italian-language sources (it)\nArticles with Italian-language sources (it)\nItaly articles missing geocoordinate data\nAll articles needing coordinates\nNavigation menu\nPersonal tools\nNot logged in\nTalk\nContributions\nCreate account\nLog in\nNamespaces\nArticle\nTalk\nVariants\nViews\nRead\nEdit\nView history\nMore\nSearch\nNavigation\nMain page\nContents\nFeatured content\nCurrent events\nRandom article\nDonate to Wikipedia\nWikipedia store\nInteraction\nHelp\nAbout Wikipedia\nCommunity portal\nRecent changes\nContact page\nTools\nWhat links here\nRelated changes\nUpload file\nSpecial pages\nPermanent link\nPage information\nWikidata item\nCite this page\nPrint/export\nCreate a book\nDownload as PDF\nPrintable version\nLanguages\nAdd links\nThis page was last edited on 8 January 2020, at 03:41 \u00a0(UTC) .\nText is available under the Creative Commons Attribution-ShareAlike License ; additional terms may apply. Wikipedia\u00ae is a registered trademark of the Wikimedia Foundation, Inc. , a non-profit organization.\nPrivacy policy\nAbout Wikipedia\nDisclaimers\nContact Wikipedia\nDevelopers\nStatistics\nCookie statement\nMobile view\n"], "_version_": 1665285020940500992, "score": 9.283754}, {"tstamp": ["2020-04-28T17:50:39.754Z"], "digest": ["7dd520c0caa6b264df3257ab4f7e3660"], "host": ["en.wikipedia.org"], "boost": [0.3873124], "id": "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_sauce", "title": ["Fettuccine Alfredo - Wikipedia"], "url": ["https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_sauce"], "content": ["Fettuccine Alfredo - Wikipedia\nFettuccine Alfredo\nFrom Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n\u00a0\u00a0(Redirected from Alfredo sauce )\nJump to navigation\nJump to search\nItalian pasta dish with butter and Parmesan cheese\nFettuccine Alfredo Course Primo (Italian pasta course) Place of origin Italy Region or state Lazio Associated national\u00a0cuisine United States Created by Alfredo di Lelio I (1882\u20131959) Main ingredients Fettuccine , butter , Parmigiano-Reggiano cheese Variations In the US \u2013 adding broccoli , cream , parsley , garlic , chicken , shrimp , turkey\nCookbook: Fettuccine Alfredo\nFettuccine Alfredo ( Italian pronunciation:\u00a0 [fettut't\u0283i\u02d0ne al\u02c8fre\u02d0do] ) [1] or fettuccine al burro [2] is an Italian\npasta dish of fresh\nfettuccine tossed with butter and Parmesan cheese ( Italian : pasta al burro e parmigiano ). [3] [4] [5] As the cheese melts, it emulsifies the liquids to form a smooth and rich sauce coating the pasta. [3] The dish is named after Alfredo di Lelio, who featured the dish at his restaurant in Rome in the early- to mid-20th century; the \"ceremony\" of preparing it tableside was an integral part of the dish. [3] [6]\nThe dish became popularized and eventually spread to the United States, where it remains popular. The recipe has evolved, and its commercialized version\u2014with heavy cream and other ingredients\u2014is now ubiquitous. In the U.S., however, it is often served as a main course , sometimes garnished with chicken or other ingredients. In Italy, meanwhile, fettuccine al burro is generally considered home cooking , in contrast to fettuccine Alfredo , a very rich version of the dish. [6]\nContents\n1\nHistory\n2\nPreparation\n3\nIn the United States\n4\nAlfredo sauce\n5\nSee also\n6\nReferences\n7\nSources\n8\nExternal links\nHistory [ edit ]\nServing fettuccine with butter and cheese was first mentioned in a 15th-century recipe for maccaroni romaneschi ('Roman pasta') by Martino da Como , a northern Italian cook active in Rome; the recipe cooks the noodles in broth or water and adds butter, \"good cheese\" (the variety is not specified) and \"sweet spices\". [7]\nModern fettuccine Alfredo was invented by Alfredo di Lelio in Rome. According to family accounts, in 1892 Alfredo di Lelio began to work in a restaurant that was located in piazza Rosa and run by his mother Angelina. Di Lelio invented \"fettuccine al triplo burro\" [3] (later named \"fettuccine all'Alfredo\" or \"fettuccine Alfredo\") in 1907 or 1908 in an effort to entice his wife, Ines, to eat after giving birth to their first child Armando. Alfredo added extra butter or \"triplo burro\u201d to the fettuccine when mixing it together for her. [8] [9] [10] Piazza Rosa disappeared in 1910 following the construction of the Galleria Colonna/Sordi and the restaurant was forced to close. Di Lelio later opened his own restaurant, Alfredo alla Scrofa then called \"Alfredo\", in 1914 on the via della Scrofa in central Rome.\nThe fame of Alfredo's fettuccine spread, first in Rome and then to other countries. Di Lelio was made a Cavaliere dell'Ordine della Corona d'Italia . [11] [12]\nIn 1943, during the war, di Lelio sold the restaurant to two of his waiters. [13] In 1950, with his son Armando, Alfredo di Lelio opened a new restaurant in piazza Augusto Imperatore, Alfredo all'Augusteo, now managed by his niece Ines Di Lelio, bringing along the famous \"gold cutlery\" [3] said to have been donated in 1927 by the American actors Mary Pickford and Douglas Fairbanks in gratitude for Alfredo's hospitality. The two restaurants competed vigorously, with escalating puffery: \"the king of fettuccine\", \"the real king of fettuccine\", \"the magician of fettuccine\", \"the emperor of fettuccine\", \"the real Alfredo\", etc. [13]\nPreparation [ edit ]\nThe dish was so well known that di Lelio was invited to demonstrate it both in Italy and abroad. [13] The fame of the dish, called on Alfredo's menus maestosissime fettuccine all'Alfredo 'most majestic fettuccine, Alfredo style', comes largely from the \"spectacle reminiscent of grand opera\" of its preparation at table, [4] as described in 1967:\n[The fettuccine] are seasoned with plenty of butter and fat parmesan, not aged, so that, in a ritual of extraordinary theatricality, the owner mixes the pasta and lifts it high to serve it, the white threads of cheese gilded with butter and the bright yellow of the ribbons of egg pasta offering an eyeful for the customer; at the end of the ceremony, the guest of honor is presented the golden cutlery and the serving dish, where the blond fettuccine roll around in the pale gold of the seasonings. It's worth seeing the whole ceremony. The owner, son of old Alfredo and looking exactly like him, ... bends over the great skein of fettuccine, fixes it intensely, his eyes half-closed, and dives into mixing it, waving the golden cutlery with grand gestures, like an orchestra conductor, with his sinister upwards-pointing twirled moustache dancing up and down, pinkies in the air, a rapt gaze, flailing elbows. [13]\nRecipes attributed to Alfredo only include three ingredients: fettuccine, young Parmesan cheese and butter. [11] [14] [13] Yet there are various legends about the \"secret\" of the original Alfredo recipe: some say oil is added to the pasta dough, others that the noodles are cooked in milk. [15] The secret may in fact be simply that the noodles, cheese and butter are tossed constantly with some pasta water in a well-warmed platter to ensure that they melt together thoroughly. [16]\nFettuccine Alfredo, minus the spectacle, has now become ubiquitous in Italian-style restaurants outside Italy, although in Italy this dish is usually called simply \"fettuccine al burro\". [5] [17]\nIn the United States [ edit ]\n\u201c\nThis act of mixing the butter and cheese through the noodles becomes quite a ceremony when performed by Alfredo in his tiny restaurant in Rome. As busy as Alfredo is with other duties, he manages to be at each table when the waiter arrives with the platter of fettuccine to be mixed by him. As a violinist plays inspiring music, Alfredo performs the sacred ceremony with a fork and spoon of solid gold. Alfredo does not cook noodles. He does not make noodles. He achieves them.\n\u201d\n\u2014\u00a0 George Rector (1933) [18]\nAlfredo's fettuccine has long been popular with Americans. By 1922, it was already being reported on by American travelers. [19] Multiple magazine articles and guidebooks in the 1920s and 1930s extolled Alfredo's noodles. [12] [20] [14] In 1927, Mary Pickford and Douglas Fairbanks supposedly dined at Alfredo's and gave him the famous gold fork and spoon. [14] Also in 1927, the American restaurateur and writer George Rector wrote up Alfredo's fettuccine and described the ceremony of its tableside preparation, accompanied by violin music, in detail; he did not give it a specific name, nor mention golden tableware. [11]\nIn the 1950s, di Lelio promoted the dish and his restaurant by putting up photos of visiting celebrities with his noodles, including Jimmy Stewart , Bob Hope , Anthony Quinn , Bing Crosby , Gary Cooper , Jack Lemmon , Ava Gardner , Tyrone Power , Sophia Loren , Cantinflas , and many others. [21]\nIn 1966, the Pennsylvania Dutch Noodle Company started marketing their dried \"Fettuccine Egg Noodles\", which included a recipe on the package for an Alfredo sauce including cream and Swiss cheese as well as Parmesan and butter. [16]\nThe American restaurant casual dining chain Olive Garden has popularized its versions of fettuccine alfredo , which may be combined with chicken, shrimp, or other foods to make main courses called \"chicken alfredo\", \"seafood alfredo\", etc. Given the strict separation of pasta and meat dishes in the usual Italian restaurant cuisine , this was never done by di Lelio. Olive Garden's recipe also includes cream and garlic. [22]\nAlfredo sauce [ edit ]\nAlfredo sauce is often sold as a convenience food in grocery stores in many countries. Unlike the original preparation, which is thickened only by cheese, the prepared food and fast food [23] versions of Alfredo may be thickened with eggs or starch .\nSee also [ edit ]\nFood portal\nList of foods named after people\nList of pasta dishes\nReferences [ edit ]\n^\n\"fettuccine\" at Collins Dictionary , accessed 2016-11-22 ( archive )\n^\nAmore, Katia (2014-10-13). \"Fettuccine al Burro or Fettuccine Alfredo\" . Wikipedia\u00ae is a registered trademark of the Wikimedia Foundation, Inc. , a non-profit organization.\nPrivacy policy\nAbout Wikipedia\nDisclaimers\nContact Wikipedia\nDevelopers\nStatistics\nCookie statement\nMobile view\n"], "_version_": 1665285020940500993, "score": 9.212539}, {"tstamp": ["2020-04-27T08:18:58.694Z"], "anchor": ["Alfredo (sauce)"], "digest": ["76b663081e41bf513e59b8c5be25ee79"], "host": ["en.wikipedia.org"], "boost": [0.013860202], "id": "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_(sauce)", "title": ["Fettuccine Alfredo - Wikipedia"], "url": ["https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_(sauce)"], "content": ["Fettuccine Alfredo - Wikipedia\nFettuccine Alfredo\nFrom Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n\u00a0\u00a0(Redirected from Alfredo (sauce) )\nJump to navigation\nJump to search\nItalian pasta dish with butter and Parmesan cheese\nFettuccine Alfredo Course Primo (Italian pasta course) Place of origin Italy Region or state Lazio Associated national\u00a0cuisine United States Created by Alfredo di Lelio I (1882\u20131959) Main ingredients Fettuccine , butter , Parmigiano-Reggiano cheese Variations In the US \u2013 adding broccoli , cream , parsley , garlic , chicken , shrimp , turkey\nCookbook: Fettuccine Alfredo\nFettuccine Alfredo ( Italian pronunciation:\u00a0 [fettut't\u0283i\u02d0ne al\u02c8fre\u02d0do] ) [1] or fettuccine al burro [2] is an Italian\npasta dish of fresh\nfettuccine tossed with butter and Parmesan cheese ( Italian : pasta al burro e parmigiano ). [3] [4] [5] As the cheese melts, it emulsifies the liquids to form a smooth and rich sauce coating the pasta. [3] The dish is named after Alfredo di Lelio, who featured the dish at his restaurant in Rome in the early- to mid-20th century; the \"ceremony\" of preparing it tableside was an integral part of the dish. [3] [6]\nThe dish became popularized and eventually spread to the United States, where it remains popular. The recipe has evolved, and its commercialized version\u2014with heavy cream and other ingredients\u2014is now ubiquitous. In the U.S., however, it is often served as a main course , sometimes garnished with chicken or other ingredients. In Italy, meanwhile, fettuccine al burro is generally considered home cooking , in contrast to fettuccine Alfredo , a very rich version of the dish. [6]\nContents\n1\nHistory\n2\nPreparation\n3\nIn the United States\n4\nAlfredo sauce\n5\nSee also\n6\nReferences\n7\nSources\n8\nExternal links\nHistory [ edit ]\nServing fettuccine with butter and cheese was first mentioned in a 15th-century recipe for maccaroni romaneschi ('Roman pasta') by Martino da Como , a northern Italian cook active in Rome; the recipe cooks the noodles in broth or water and adds butter, \"good cheese\" (the variety is not specified) and \"sweet spices\". [7]\nModern fettuccine Alfredo was invented by Alfredo di Lelio in Rome. According to family accounts, in 1892 Alfredo di Lelio began to work in a restaurant that was located in piazza Rosa and run by his mother Angelina. Di Lelio invented \"fettuccine al triplo burro\" [3] (later named \"fettuccine all'Alfredo\" or \"fettuccine Alfredo\") in 1907 or 1908 in an effort to entice his wife, Ines, to eat after giving birth to their first child Armando. Alfredo added extra butter or \"triplo burro\u201d to the fettuccine when mixing it together for her. [8] [9] [10] Piazza Rosa disappeared in 1910 following the construction of the Galleria Colonna/Sordi and the restaurant was forced to close. Di Lelio later opened his own restaurant, Alfredo alla Scrofa then called \"Alfredo\", in 1914 on the via della Scrofa in central Rome.\nThe fame of Alfredo's fettuccine spread, first in Rome and then to other countries. Di Lelio was made a Cavaliere dell'Ordine della Corona d'Italia . [11] [12]\nIn 1943, during the war, di Lelio sold the restaurant to two of his waiters. [13] In 1950, with his son Armando, Alfredo di Lelio opened a new restaurant in piazza Augusto Imperatore, Alfredo all'Augusteo, now managed by his niece Ines Di Lelio, bringing along the famous \"gold cutlery\" [3] said to have been donated in 1927 by the American actors Mary Pickford and Douglas Fairbanks in gratitude for Alfredo's hospitality. The two restaurants competed vigorously, with escalating puffery: \"the king of fettuccine\", \"the real king of fettuccine\", \"the magician of fettuccine\", \"the emperor of fettuccine\", \"the real Alfredo\", etc. [13]\nPreparation [ edit ]\nThe dish was so well known that di Lelio was invited to demonstrate it both in Italy and abroad. [13] The fame of the dish, called on Alfredo's menus maestosissime fettuccine all'Alfredo 'most majestic fettuccine, Alfredo style', comes largely from the \"spectacle reminiscent of grand opera\" of its preparation at table, [4] as described in 1967:\n[The fettuccine] are seasoned with plenty of butter and fat parmesan, not aged, so that, in a ritual of extraordinary theatricality, the owner mixes the pasta and lifts it high to serve it, the white threads of cheese gilded with butter and the bright yellow of the ribbons of egg pasta offering an eyeful for the customer; at the end of the ceremony, the guest of honor is presented the golden cutlery and the serving dish, where the blond fettuccine roll around in the pale gold of the seasonings. It's worth seeing the whole ceremony. The owner, son of old Alfredo and looking exactly like him, ... bends over the great skein of fettuccine, fixes it intensely, his eyes half-closed, and dives into mixing it, waving the golden cutlery with grand gestures, like an orchestra conductor, with his sinister upwards-pointing twirled moustache dancing up and down, pinkies in the air, a rapt gaze, flailing elbows. [13]\nRecipes attributed to Alfredo only include three ingredients: fettuccine, young Parmesan cheese and butter. [11] [14] [13] Yet there are various legends about the \"secret\" of the original Alfredo recipe: some say oil is added to the pasta dough, others that the noodles are cooked in milk. [15] The secret may in fact be simply that the noodles, cheese and butter are tossed constantly with some pasta water in a well-warmed platter to ensure that they melt together thoroughly. [16]\nFettuccine Alfredo, minus the spectacle, has now become ubiquitous in Italian-style restaurants outside Italy, although in Italy this dish is usually called simply \"fettuccine al burro\". [5] [17]\nIn the United States [ edit ]\n\u201c\nThis act of mixing the butter and cheese through the noodles becomes quite a ceremony when performed by Alfredo in his tiny restaurant in Rome. As busy as Alfredo is with other duties, he manages to be at each table when the waiter arrives with the platter of fettuccine to be mixed by him. As a violinist plays inspiring music, Alfredo performs the sacred ceremony with a fork and spoon of solid gold. Alfredo does not cook noodles. He does not make noodles. He achieves them.\n\u201d\n\u2014\u00a0 George Rector (1933) [18]\nAlfredo's fettuccine has long been popular with Americans. By 1922, it was already being reported on by American travelers. [19] Multiple magazine articles and guidebooks in the 1920s and 1930s extolled Alfredo's noodles. [12] [20] [14] In 1927, Mary Pickford and Douglas Fairbanks supposedly dined at Alfredo's and gave him the famous gold fork and spoon. [14] Also in 1927, the American restaurateur and writer George Rector wrote up Alfredo's fettuccine and described the ceremony of its tableside preparation, accompanied by violin music, in detail; he did not give it a specific name, nor mention golden tableware. [11]\nIn the 1950s, di Lelio promoted the dish and his restaurant by putting up photos of visiting celebrities with his noodles, including Jimmy Stewart , Bob Hope , Anthony Quinn , Bing Crosby , Gary Cooper , Jack Lemmon , Ava Gardner , Tyrone Power , Sophia Loren , Cantinflas , and many others. [21]\nIn 1966, the Pennsylvania Dutch Noodle Company started marketing their dried \"Fettuccine Egg Noodles\", which included a recipe on the package for an Alfredo sauce including cream and Swiss cheese as well as Parmesan and butter. [16]\nThe American restaurant casual dining chain Olive Garden has popularized its versions of fettuccine alfredo , which may be combined with chicken, shrimp, or other foods to make main courses called \"chicken alfredo\", \"seafood alfredo\", etc. Given the strict separation of pasta and meat dishes in the usual Italian restaurant cuisine , this was never done by di Lelio. Olive Garden's recipe also includes cream and garlic. [22]\nAlfredo sauce [ edit ]\nAlfredo sauce is often sold as a convenience food in grocery stores in many countries. Unlike the original preparation, which is thickened only by cheese, the prepared food and fast food [23] versions of Alfredo may be thickened with eggs or starch .\nSee also [ edit ]\nFood portal\nList of foods named after people\nList of pasta dishes\nReferences [ edit ]\n^\n\"fettuccine\" at Collins Dictionary , accessed 2016-11-22 ( archive )\n^\nAmore, Katia (2014-10-13). \"Fettuccine al Burro or Fettuccine Alfredo\" . Wikipedia\u00ae is a registered trademark of the Wikimedia Foundation, Inc. , a non-profit organization.\nPrivacy policy\nAbout Wikipedia\nDisclaimers\nContact Wikipedia\nDevelopers\nStatistics\nCookie statement\nMobile view\n"], "_version_": 1665142691637231618, "score": 9.204982}, {"tstamp": ["2020-04-28T15:48:55.023Z"], "digest": ["c45071604722ba7a180846b5cbb2c0bc"], "host": ["en.wikipedia.org"], "boost": [0.3873124], "id": "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fettuccine_Alfredo", "title": ["Fettuccine Alfredo - Wikipedia"], "url": ["https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fettuccine_Alfredo"], "content": ["Fettuccine Alfredo - Wikipedia\nFettuccine Alfredo\nFrom Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\nJump to navigation\nJump to search\nItalian pasta dish with butter and Parmesan cheese\nFettuccine Alfredo Course Primo (Italian pasta course) Place of origin Italy Region or state Lazio Associated national\u00a0cuisine United States Created by Alfredo di Lelio I (1882\u20131959) Main ingredients Fettuccine , butter , Parmigiano-Reggiano cheese Variations In the US \u2013 adding broccoli , cream , parsley , garlic , chicken , shrimp , turkey\nCookbook: Fettuccine Alfredo\nFettuccine Alfredo ( Italian pronunciation:\u00a0 [fettut't\u0283i\u02d0ne al\u02c8fre\u02d0do] ) [1] or fettuccine al burro [2] is an Italian\npasta dish of fresh\nfettuccine tossed with butter and Parmesan cheese ( Italian : pasta al burro e parmigiano ). [3] [4] [5] As the cheese melts, it emulsifies the liquids to form a smooth and rich sauce coating the pasta. [3] The dish is named after Alfredo di Lelio, who featured the dish at his restaurant in Rome in the early- to mid-20th century; the \"ceremony\" of preparing it tableside was an integral part of the dish. [3] [6]\nThe dish became popularized and eventually spread to the United States, where it remains popular. The recipe has evolved, and its commercialized version\u2014with heavy cream and other ingredients\u2014is now ubiquitous. In the U.S., however, it is often served as a main course , sometimes garnished with chicken or other ingredients. In Italy, meanwhile, fettuccine al burro is generally considered home cooking , in contrast to fettuccine Alfredo , a very rich version of the dish. [6]\nContents\n1\nHistory\n2\nPreparation\n3\nIn the United States\n4\nAlfredo sauce\n5\nSee also\n6\nReferences\n7\nSources\n8\nExternal links\nHistory [ edit ]\nServing fettuccine with butter and cheese was first mentioned in a 15th-century recipe for maccaroni romaneschi ('Roman pasta') by Martino da Como , a northern Italian cook active in Rome; the recipe cooks the noodles in broth or water and adds butter, \"good cheese\" (the variety is not specified) and \"sweet spices\". [7]\nModern fettuccine Alfredo was invented by Alfredo di Lelio in Rome. According to family accounts, in 1892 Alfredo di Lelio began to work in a restaurant that was located in piazza Rosa and run by his mother Angelina. Di Lelio invented \"fettuccine al triplo burro\" [3] (later named \"fettuccine all'Alfredo\" or \"fettuccine Alfredo\") in 1907 or 1908 in an effort to entice his wife, Ines, to eat after giving birth to their first child Armando. Alfredo added extra butter or \"triplo burro\u201d to the fettuccine when mixing it together for her. [8] [9] [10] Piazza Rosa disappeared in 1910 following the construction of the Galleria Colonna/Sordi and the restaurant was forced to close. Di Lelio later opened his own restaurant, Alfredo alla Scrofa then called \"Alfredo\", in 1914 on the via della Scrofa in central Rome.\nThe fame of Alfredo's fettuccine spread, first in Rome and then to other countries. Di Lelio was made a Cavaliere dell'Ordine della Corona d'Italia . [11] [12]\nIn 1943, during the war, di Lelio sold the restaurant to two of his waiters. [13] In 1950, with his son Armando, Alfredo di Lelio opened a new restaurant in piazza Augusto Imperatore, Alfredo all'Augusteo, now managed by his niece Ines Di Lelio, bringing along the famous \"gold cutlery\" [3] said to have been donated in 1927 by the American actors Mary Pickford and Douglas Fairbanks in gratitude for Alfredo's hospitality. The two restaurants competed vigorously, with escalating puffery: \"the king of fettuccine\", \"the real king of fettuccine\", \"the magician of fettuccine\", \"the emperor of fettuccine\", \"the real Alfredo\", etc. [13]\nPreparation [ edit ]\nThe dish was so well known that di Lelio was invited to demonstrate it both in Italy and abroad. [13] The fame of the dish, called on Alfredo's menus maestosissime fettuccine all'Alfredo 'most majestic fettuccine, Alfredo style', comes largely from the \"spectacle reminiscent of grand opera\" of its preparation at table, [4] as described in 1967:\n[The fettuccine] are seasoned with plenty of butter and fat parmesan, not aged, so that, in a ritual of extraordinary theatricality, the owner mixes the pasta and lifts it high to serve it, the white threads of cheese gilded with butter and the bright yellow of the ribbons of egg pasta offering an eyeful for the customer; at the end of the ceremony, the guest of honor is presented the golden cutlery and the serving dish, where the blond fettuccine roll around in the pale gold of the seasonings. It's worth seeing the whole ceremony. The owner, son of old Alfredo and looking exactly like him, ... bends over the great skein of fettuccine, fixes it intensely, his eyes half-closed, and dives into mixing it, waving the golden cutlery with grand gestures, like an orchestra conductor, with his sinister upwards-pointing twirled moustache dancing up and down, pinkies in the air, a rapt gaze, flailing elbows. [13]\nRecipes attributed to Alfredo only include three ingredients: fettuccine, young Parmesan cheese and butter. [11] [14] [13] Yet there are various legends about the \"secret\" of the original Alfredo recipe: some say oil is added to the pasta dough, others that the noodles are cooked in milk. [15] The secret may in fact be simply that the noodles, cheese and butter are tossed constantly with some pasta water in a well-warmed platter to ensure that they melt together thoroughly. [16]\nFettuccine Alfredo, minus the spectacle, has now become ubiquitous in Italian-style restaurants outside Italy, although in Italy this dish is usually called simply \"fettuccine al burro\". [5] [17]\nIn the United States [ edit ]\n\u201c\nThis act of mixing the butter and cheese through the noodles becomes quite a ceremony when performed by Alfredo in his tiny restaurant in Rome. As busy as Alfredo is with other duties, he manages to be at each table when the waiter arrives with the platter of fettuccine to be mixed by him. As a violinist plays inspiring music, Alfredo performs the sacred ceremony with a fork and spoon of solid gold. Alfredo does not cook noodles. He does not make noodles. He achieves them.\n\u201d\n\u2014\u00a0 George Rector (1933) [18]\nAlfredo's fettuccine has long been popular with Americans. By 1922, it was already being reported on by American travelers. [19] Multiple magazine articles and guidebooks in the 1920s and 1930s extolled Alfredo's noodles. [12] [20] [14] In 1927, Mary Pickford and Douglas Fairbanks supposedly dined at Alfredo's and gave him the famous gold fork and spoon. [14] Also in 1927, the American restaurateur and writer George Rector wrote up Alfredo's fettuccine and described the ceremony of its tableside preparation, accompanied by violin music, in detail; he did not give it a specific name, nor mention golden tableware. [11]\nIn the 1950s, di Lelio promoted the dish and his restaurant by putting up photos of visiting celebrities with his noodles, including Jimmy Stewart , Bob Hope , Anthony Quinn , Bing Crosby , Gary Cooper , Jack Lemmon , Ava Gardner , Tyrone Power , Sophia Loren , Cantinflas , and many others. [21]\nIn 1966, the Pennsylvania Dutch Noodle Company started marketing their dried \"Fettuccine Egg Noodles\", which included a recipe on the package for an Alfredo sauce including cream and Swiss cheese as well as Parmesan and butter. [16]\nThe American restaurant casual dining chain Olive Garden has popularized its versions of fettuccine alfredo , which may be combined with chicken, shrimp, or other foods to make main courses called \"chicken alfredo\", \"seafood alfredo\", etc. Given the strict separation of pasta and meat dishes in the usual Italian restaurant cuisine , this was never done by di Lelio. Olive Garden's recipe also includes cream and garlic. [22]\nAlfredo sauce [ edit ]\nAlfredo sauce is often sold as a convenience food in grocery stores in many countries. Unlike the original preparation, which is thickened only by cheese, the prepared food and fast food [23] versions of Alfredo may be thickened with eggs or starch .\nSee also [ edit ]\nFood portal\nList of foods named after people\nList of pasta dishes\nReferences [ edit ]\n^\n\"fettuccine\" at Collins Dictionary , accessed 2016-11-22 ( archive )\n^\nAmore, Katia (2014-10-13). \"Fettuccine al Burro or Fettuccine Alfredo\" . This is a meal the entire family will go crazy for!\nIf you are looking for more ways to make amazing pasta, be sure to use The Best Homemade Alfredo Sauce Ever or Skinny Garlic Alfredo Sauce . You won\u2019t need another recipe!\nGarlic Alfredo Pasta\nMy kids love the Olive Garden. I totally get it. It isn\u2019t the best authentic Italian that I have ever had, but they do have some pretty amazing alfredo. My son ordered the Asiago Garlic Alfredo the last time we went. Asiago Garlic Alfredo?? I knew that I needed to come home and immediately make it for ourselves. My Alfredo Recipe is so much better than Olive Garden and I knew that adding Asiago cheese would take it to the next level.\nI know that my recipe has cream cheese in it, but I am a strong believer that that is the secret of making this sauce ultra rich and creamy. I love when it just coats the noodles perfectly and is so creamy with each and every bite! There is a reason why my alfredo sauce is one of the most searched recipes in the world!\nHow do you make homemade alfredo sauce?\nYou start by melting the butter. Whisk in the heavy cream and cream cheese. Cook over medium heat and whisk until melted. Add the minced garlic, garlic powder, Italian Seasoning, and salt and pepper. Whisk until smooth. Add the freshly grated asiago cheese.\nHow do you make alfredo sauce from the Olive Garden?\nTraditionally alfredo sauce from the olive garden includes cream, garlic, and parmesan cheese. This recipe includes a few more things but is so much better!\nWhat sides can I serve with Alfredo Garlic Pasta?\nClassic Caesar Salad\nCheesy Cheddar Garlic Breadsticks\u00a0\nBreadsticks\nGreen Engish Peas\nBroccoli\n\u00a0\n\u00a0\nAsiago Garlic Alfredo Pasta\n5 from 4 votes\nPrep Time\n5\nminutes\nCook Time\n10\nminutes\nTotal Time\n15\nminutes\nAuthor\nAlyssa Rivers\nPrint\nReview\nAsiago Garlic Alfredo Pasta gets tossed in the best creamy and rich asiago garlic alfredo! This is a meal the entire family will go crazy for!\nCourse\nMain Course\nIngredients\n1\npound\nfettuccine pasta\nor pasta of choice\n\u00bd\ncup\nbutter\n1-\npint\nheavy whipping cream\n2 cups\n4\nounces\ncream cheese\n\u00bd\nteaspoon\nminced garlic\n1\nteaspoon\ngarlic powder\n1\nteaspoon\nItalian seasoning\n\u00bc\nteaspoon\nsalt\n\u00bc\nteaspoon\npepper\n1\ncup\nAsiago cheese\nInstructions\nIn a large pot of boiling water, cook pasta according to package directions until al dente.\nIn a medium saucepan add butter, heavy whipping cream, and cream cheese. Cook over medium heat and whisk until melted. Add the minced garlic, garlic powder,\nitalian\nseasoning, salt, and pepper. Continue to whisk until smooth. Add the grated asiago cheese.\nBring to a simmer and continue to cook for about 3-5 minutes or until it starts to thicken. Toss it with your favorite pasta!\nShare The Post!\nShare on Facebook 0 Pin on Pinterest 0 Share via Email 0\nGet free recipes to your inbox!\nPlease enable JavaScript in your browser to complete this form.\nYour First Name *\nYour Email Address *\nEmail\nSubmit\nAlyssa Rivers\nI am Alyssa and the blogger behind The Recipe Critic. Barcelona\nOur Wedding\nAlfredo Sauce\nJump To Recipe\n9 Comments \u00bb\nThis post may contain affiliate links. Please read my disclosure policy .\nMy favorite recipe for homemade Alfredo sauce.\u00a0 It\u2019s easy to make in just 15 minutes, full of the best creamy and garlicky flavors, and always ultra comforting and delicious.\nAfter sharing my favorite marinara sauce recipe with you yesterday, today I\u2019m sharing my go-to recipe for its creamy, cheesy, ultra-comforting counterpart\u2026\n\u2026my favorite homemade Alfredo sauce. \u2661\nNow I will be the first to note that this Alfredo sauce recipe is \u201cAmerican-style,\u201d a la the Olive Garden version that zillions of us grew up loving.\u00a0 By contrast to its Italian-style origins, in which the sauce was created in Rome with just butter and cheese (more similar to my cacio e pepe recipe ), American-style Alfredo sauce is famously a bit more indulgent and complex.\u00a0 Heavy cream and/or milk are typically added to make the sauce creamier, differing levels of flour are added to create a roux and make the sauce thicker, and a number of different seasonings are often added (especially a hint of white pepper and nutmeg) to give it an extra flavor boost.\u00a0 So while this may come as a surprise to some, the American-style version of this sauce would definitely not be considered authentic in Italy.\u00a0 But hey, I think we can all agree that the creamy version of this sauce has become an iconic favorite of its own. \u2661\nThat said, though, all American-style Alfredo sauce recipes are\u00a0 definitely not created alike!\u00a0 I don\u2019t know about you guys, but I have been served far too many Alfredos over the years that were gloppy and greasy and devoid of good flavor, which simply will not do.\u00a0 (Especially when indulging in a cream sauce\u2026I want it to be amazing!)\u00a0 So today, I\u2019m sharing my favorite homemade Alfredo recipe that I have tweaked over the years to perfection.\nMy version is made with a base of half milk and half cream, so that it\u2019s still rich and creamy but not overly heavy.\u00a0 It\u2019s seasoned with plenty of garlic plus a hint of white pepper and nutmeg, all of which serve to balance out those creamy flavors nicely.\u00a0 It\u2019s just slightly thickened with a tablespoon of flour, which you are also welcome to leave out entirely if you prefer.\u00a0 And best of all, it\u2019s made with lots and lots of freshly-grated Parmesan, which is really the main flavor we all want and love in a good Alfredo.\nOh and bonus?\u00a0 The entire recipe is incredibly easy to make and comes together in just 15 minutes.\u00a0 And, of course, it tastes a million times better than anything that you can buy in a jar.\u00a0 Perfect for tossing with pasta, topping grilled chicken, spreading as a white pizza sauce, mixing into lasagna and baked ziti, or whatever else sounds good.\nI\u2019m telling you, this Alfredo sauce is always a winner.\u00a0 So let\u2019s make some!\nAlfredo Sauce Recipe | 1-Minute Video\nHomemade Alfredo Sauce Ingredients:\nTo make this American-style Alfredo sauce recipe, you will need the following ingredients:\nButter:\u00a0 Or you could also substitute olive oil, if you prefer.\nGarlic:\u00a0 Finely-minced or pressed.\nAll-purpose flour:\u00a0 To help form a roux and thicken the sauce.\u00a0 If you are making gluten-free Alfredo sauce, however, you are welcome to omit the flour and have a slightly thinner sauce.\u00a0 Or you can use a cornstarch slurry to thicken it (see details below).\nHeavy cream and milk:\u00a0 We will use this blend as the base for our sauce.\nParmesan cheese:\u00a0 I recommend freshly-grating your Parmesan cheese so that it will melt more smoothly into the sauce.\u00a0 Also, grated Parmesan cheese can be tricky to measure correctly simply with a measuring cup, so I recommend using a kitchen scale if you own one.\nSea salt and white pepper :\u00a0 I like to use fine sea salt and white pepper to season this sauce.\u00a0 If you are new to cooking with white pepper, please note that it has a slightly different flavor and is significantly more potent than black pepper, so you do not need to use as much.\u00a0 That said, if you only have black pepper in the house, that will work too.\nGround nutmeg : \u00a0A pinch of nutmeg is typically used in American-style Alfredo, but you can omit this if you prefer.\nHow To Make Alfredo Sauce:\nAlright, let\u2019s talk about how to make Alfredo sauce!\u00a0 Simply\u2026\nSaut\u00e9 garlic.\u00a0 Briefly saut\u00e9 the garlic in butter until it is lightly golden (be sure not to overcook it).\u00a0 Then stir in some flour to form a roux.\nAdd the milk and cream.\u00a0\u00a0 And whisk until evenly combined.\nSimmer. Continue cooking the sauce until it reaches a simmer, then reduce heat to maintain the simmer, add in the Parmesan, salt, white pepper and nutmeg, and whisk until the cheese is completely melted and the sauce is smooth.\nSeason. Don\u2019t forget to taste and season with extra salt and/or white pepper, if needed.\nServe.\u00a0\u00a0 And\u2026enjoy!\u00a0 So simple, right?!\nPossible Recipe Variations:\nThere are all sorts of ways that you can customize this basic Alfredo sauce recipe, so feel free to experiment and get creative!\u00a0 Here are a few of my favorite variations\u2026\nMake it gluten-free:\u00a0 To make gluten-free Alfredo sauce, just omit the flour (and have a slightly thinner sauce).\u00a0 Or, you can omit the flour and use a cornstarch slurry (equal parts cold water and cornstarch, added to the sauce as it is simmering) to thicken the sauce.\nMake it lighter: To make a lighter Alfredo sauce, use milk in place of heavy cream (so 2 cups of milk total, no cream).\nMake it extra-garlicky:\u00a0 If you want to make your sauce extra-garlicky, feel free to double the amount of garlic cloves.\nUse roasted garlic: If you want even more complex garlic flavors in the sauce, skip the minced garlic and instead roast an entire head of garlic and stir the cloves into the sauce to make a delicious roasted garlic Alfredo sauce.\nAdd Cajun seasoning:\u00a0 To make Cajun Alfredo sauce, stir your desired amount of Cajun seasoning (I recommend 2 to 4 teaspoons, to taste) into the sauce.\nAdd pesto:\u00a0 If you happen to have some basil pesto on hand, try stirring in a few tablespoons to make a delicious pesto Alfredo sauce.\nWays To Use Alfredo Sauce:\nThere are endless ways that you can put this Alfredo sauce recipe to delicious use!\u00a0 For example, feel free to make\u2026\nAlfredo Pasta: Fettuccine Alfredo is obviously the most famous option here, but any shape of pasta will do.\u00a0 To make traditional fettuccine Alfredo, cook 1 pound of fettuccine until al dente, drain, then toss with the Alfredo sauce until combined.\u00a0 Feel free to add in cooked proteins of your choice (for example, to make chicken Alfredo pasta, shrimp Alfredo, or meatballs Alfredo).\u00a0 And of course, veggies such as broccoli, mushrooms, asparagus and more are delicious additions too!\nHomemade Pasta Option: Or, if you really want to kick your Alfredo pasta up a notch, try making it with homemade pasta! One batch of this sauce will pair perfectly with one batch of my favorite homemade pasta recipe .\nAlfredo Pizza:\u00a0 Use this sauce in place of marinara pizza sauce.\nAlfredo Dip:\u00a0 Use this sauce as a dip for breadsticks, veggie sticks, pretzels and more.\nAlfredo Casserole:\u00a0 I also love using this recipe as a sauce in casseroles , baked ziti and white lasagna.\nMore Italian Sauce Recipes:\nLooking to try some other classic Italian sauces?\u00a0 Here are a few of my faves:\nBasil Pesto\nCacio e Pepe\nMarinara Sauce\nSpicy Arrabbiata Sauce\nAglio e Olio (Garlic and Olive Oil) Sauce\nPrint\nAlfredo Sauce\n\u2605 \u2605 \u2605 \u2605 \u2605\n5 from 2 reviews\nAuthor:\nAli\nPrep Time:\n5 mins\nCook Time:\n10 mins\nTotal Time:\n15 mins\nYield:\nAbout 2.5 cup s 1 x\nPrint\nPin\nDescription\nThis homemade Alfredo sauce recipe is easy to make in just 15 minutes, it\u2019s rich and creamy and full of the best garlicky flavors, and always ultra comforting and delicious.\u00a0 See notes above for possible variations too.\nScale\n1x 2x 3x\nIngredients\n1 tablespoon butter\n4 \u00a0cloves garlic, pressed or finely-minced\n1 tablespoon all-purpose flour\n1 cup heavy cream\n1 cup milk (I used 2% milk)\n1 cup ( 1 1/2 ounce s) freshly-grated Parmesan cheese\n1/2 teaspoon\nfine sea salt\npinch of white pepper\npinch of ground nutmeg (optional)\nInstructions\nSaut\u00e9 garlic.\u00a0 Melt butter in a large saucepan or saut\u00e9 pan over medium-high heat.\u00a0 Add garlic and saut\u00e9 for 1 minute, stirring frequently.\u00a0 Stir in the flour and saut\u00e9 for 1 minute more, stirring frequently.\nAdd the milk and cream.\u00a0 Add in the heavy cream and milk and whisk until evenly combined.\nSimmer. Continue cooking until the mixture reaches a simmer.\u00a0 Reduce heat to medium-low and continue cooking for 1-2 minutes, until thickened.\u00a0 Add in the Parmesan, salt, white pepper and nutmeg, and whisk until the cheese is completely melted and the sauce is smooth.\nSeason.\u00a0 Taste and season with extra salt and/or white pepper, if needed.\nServe.\u00a0\u00a0 Serve warm and enjoy!\nEquipment\nGround Nutmeg\nBuy Now \u2192\nFine Sea Salt\nBuy Now \u2192\nWhite Pepper\nBuy Now \u2192\nNotes\nBatch Amount: This recipe yields enough sauce to toss with a 1-pound (or 500g) package of uncooked pasta, which should be cooked until al dente, drained and then immediately tossed with the sauce.\nStorage Instructions:\u00a0 To store this Alfredo sauce, let it cool until it reaches room temperature.\u00a0 Then transfer to a mason jar or food storage container and refrigerate for up to 3 days.\u00a0 I do not recommend freezing this sauce.\nDid you make this recipe?\nTag @gimmesomeoven on Instagram and hashtag it #gimmesomeoven\nposted on April 8, 2020 in Italian , Sauces , Vegetarian\n9 Comments \u00bb\nShare this Post\nYou May Also Like...\nSeed Cycling Energy Bites\nFlourless Chocolate Chip Cookies\nCan\u2019t-Believe-It\u2019s-Vegetarian Chili\nLeave a Reply Cancel reply\nYour email address will not be published. All rights reserved.\nHome\nRecipes\nGeoffrey Zakarian\nPrev Recipe\nNext Recipe\nWATCH\nWATCH\nLoading Video...\nSee more\n(12)\nFettuccine Alfredo\nRecipe courtesy of Geoffrey Zakarian\nRecipe courtesy of Geoffrey Zakarian\nShow:\nThe Kitchen\nEpisode:\nWinter Fix\nFettuccine Alfredo\nGetting reviews...\nSave Recipe\nLevel:\nEasy\nTotal:\n30 min\nActive:\n30 min\nYield:\n4 servings\nShare This Recipe\nPinterest\nFacebook\nTwitter\nEmail\nLevel:\nEasy\nTotal:\n30 min\nActive:\n30 min\nYield:\n4 servings\nIngredients\nBechamel:\n4 tablespoons butter\n5 tablespoons all-purpose flour\u00a0\n1/4 teaspoon ground cloves\nPinch grated nutmeg\u00a0\n2 1/2 cups whole milk, warmed\nKosher salt and freshly ground black pepper\nFettuccine Alfredo:\nKosher salt and freshly ground black pepper\n12 ounces dried fettuccine\u00a0\n2 tablespoons olive oil\u00a0\n1/2 cup thinly sliced shallots\u00a0\n2 cloves garlic, finely minced\u00a0\n1/2 cup grated Parmigiano-Reggiano\u00a0\n1/2 cup grated Pecorino Romano cheese\n1/4 cup finely minced fresh parsley\nDirections\nWATCH\nWatch how to make this recipe.\nFor the bechamel: In a medium saucepan, melt the butter over medium flame. Add the flour and whisk until the texture of wet sand is achieved. Lower the heat to low, add the cloves and nutmeg and cook for 2 minutes. Slowly whisk in the whole milk and bring the sauce to a simmer. Cook for 3 minutes, season with salt and pepper and set aside.\nFor the fettuccine alfredo: Bring a large pot of water to a boil and season with salt. Add the pasta and begin to cook.\nMeanwhile, in a large saute pan, heat the olive oil over medium heat. Cook the shallots and garlic until soft, about 4 minutes. Add the bechamel sauce, along with 1 cup of the pasta water.\nWhen the pasta is 80 percent cooked, add it to the saute pan and simmer until the sauce is thickened and the pasta is al dente. Toss with the cheeses and parsley, and season with salt and pepper.\nMy Private Notes\nAdd a Note\nWATCH\nShow:\nThe Kitchen\nEpisode:\nWinter Fix\nCategories:\nAlfredo\nMain Dish\nVegetarian\nMore from:\nThe Kitchen\nLooking for Something Else?\nQuick & Easy\nMore Cheese Recipes\n5 Ingredients or Less\nHighly Rated\nChicken Fettuccine Alfredo\nShrimp Fettuccine Alfredo\nFettuccine Alfredo\nFettuccine Alfredo\nChicken Fettuccine Alfredo\nLow-Cal Fettuccine Alfredo\nSpring Vegetable Fettuccine Alfredo\nChicken Alfredo Stuffed Shells\nGet the Food Network Kitchen App\n\ud83d\udc69\u200d\ud83c\udf73 What's Cooking\nHealthy Dinners \u2014 Fast!\nTop Cauliflower Recipes\n60+ Spring Dinners\nDiscover More Recipes...\nLet's Get Cooking!\nTo sign up, please enable JavaScript.\nSign up for the Recipe of the Day newsletter to receive editor-picked recipes, tips and videos delivered to your inbox daily. Please read my disclosure policy .\nThis Chicken Alfredo Baked Ziti recipe is made with a lightened-up alfredo sauce, it\u2019s easy to customize with extra veggies and seasonings, and it is always so comforting and delicious.\nCreamy, cozy, cheesy, carb-y comfort food alert. \u2661\nThis time of year, when everyone seems to be craving warm pasta dinners around the table on chilly winter nights, this chicken alfredo baked ziti recipe always goes viral here on the blog.\u00a0 And this time of year, when I make a batch for myself, I\u2019m always reminded how unbeatable this Italian casserole will always be.\u00a0 I mean, creamy alfredo sauce, savory chicken, hearty pasta, two delicious kinds of melty cheese \u2014 what\u2019s not to love?!\u00a0 There\u2019s a reason why this one will always be a classic.\nThat said, while this recipe already features my lightened-up alfredo sauce recipe, there are all sorts of other ways you can make this comfort food a bit healthier if you\u2019d like.\u00a0 From subbing in whole wheat pasta ( this one \u00a0is my go-to), to adding in your choice of veggies (we\u2019re quite partial to broccoli in our house), to making it all gluten-free if you\u2019d like (easy to do with a few simple tweaks), options to customize this casserole abound.\u00a0 And bonus, it can be ready to serve a big crowd in less than 45 minutes.\nWho\u2019s ready for a helping?\nMy original photo for this recipe from 2014.\nChicken Alfredo Baked Ziti Ingredients:\nTo make this Chicken Alfredo Baked Ziti recipe, you will need:\nPasta:\u00a0 Feel free to use any shape (ziti, penne, fettuccine, etc.) and variety (classic, whole-wheat , gluten-free, etc.) of pasta that you prefer.\nShredded, cooked chicken:\u00a0 I either shred a rotisserie chicken, or use leftovers from this baked chicken breasts recipe.\nShredded mozzarella cheese:\u00a0 Feel free to use part-skim or full-fat.\nAlfredo sauce:\u00a0 We will use my lightened-up alfredo sauce recipe, made simply with olive oil (or butter), garlic, flour, chicken stock, low-fat milk, Parmesan, salt and pepper.\u00a0 Also, this recipe is not naturally very saucy.\u00a0 So if you would like, many of our readers recommend doubling the sauce .\nToppings:\u00a0 Freshly-grated Parmesan is a must, in my book.\u00a0 And feel free to sprinkle on some chopped parsley for extra freshness and flavor.\nAlso, see below for suggestions on other delicious ingredients you can add in to this easy baked ziti.\u00a0 (Here\u2019s lookin\u2019 at you, broccoli and Cajun seasoning. \u2661 )\nHow To Make Chicken Alfredo Baked Ziti:\nAlright, let\u2019s talk about how to make baked ziti!\u00a0 Simply\u2026\nPrepare\u00a0the alfredo sauce.\u00a0\u00a0 To make the alfredo recipe, just saut\u00e9 some garlic in olive oil (or butter).\u00a0 Stir in some flour to thicken, add stock and milk and bring to a simmer.\u00a0 Then stir in the Parmesan, season with salt and pepper, and you\u2019re ready to go!\nCook the pasta (and chicken).\u00a0\u00a0 Meanwhile, do some multi-tasking and cook your pasta according to package instructions in a large pot of generously-salted water.\u00a0 Also, if you are cooking your chicken from scratch (vs. using leftovers or shredding a rotisserie), go ahead and cook it while the pasta and sauce are being prepared.\nLayer everything together.\u00a0 Once your pasta, sauce, and chicken are all ready to go, it\u2019s time to combine everything!\u00a0 In your pasta pot, stir together the pasta, alfredo sauce and chicken until combined.\u00a0 Then spread half of the pasta mixture out evenly in a 9 x 13-inch baking dish.\u00a0 Sprinkle on half of the mozzarella.\u00a0 And repeat with the remaining pasta mixture, and remaining half of the mozzarella.\nBake.\u00a0 Transfer the pan to the oven and bake (uncovered) for 20 minutes, or until the cheese is completely melted and has started to brown a bit on top.\nAdd toppings.\u00a0\u00a0 Remove and sprinkle with lots of freshly-grated Parmesan and finely-chopped fresh parsley, if desired.\nServe.\u00a0\u00a0 Then dish it up while it\u2019s still nice and warm, and enjoy!\nPossible Variations:\nThere are\u00a0so many ways to customize this chicken alfredo bake!\u00a0 For example, feel free to\u2026\nAdd in veggies.\u00a0 Broccoli, asparagus, mushrooms, cauliflower, and any number of other veggies\u00a0would be delicious added to this chicken alfredo recipe.\u00a0 Just note that they won\u2019t get cooked much during the 20 minutes of baking time.\u00a0 So if whatever veggies you add require a longer cooking time, feel free to toss them into the boiling water with the pasta for a few minutes or saut\u00e9 (or roast) them for a few minutes before adding them to the casserole.\nAdd in extra Italian herbs.\u00a0 If you would like an herbier chicken alfredo pasta, feel free to add some dried Italian seasoning or chopped fresh Italian herbs into the alfredo sauce.\u00a0 (Or, you can also sprinkle some chopped fresh basil on top of the pasta after baking.)\nNix the protein.\u00a0 Not into chicken?\u00a0 Feel free to use shrimp in this recipe instead.\u00a0 (Or make it vegetarian and add in some extra veggies instead.)\nMake it spicy.\u00a0 I really love\u00a0sprinkling lots of crushed red pepper into (and on top of) this casserole to give it a bit of a kick.\nMake it cajun.\u00a0 To give this recipe a Cajun twist, feel free to\u00a0stir 1-2 tablespoons Cajun seasoning (to taste) into the alfredo sauce.\nMake it gluten-free.\u00a0\u00a0 Just use your favorite certified gluten-free pasta, and my gluten-free alfredo sauce recipe .\nRecommended Side Dishes:\nTo balance out this chicken alfredo baked ziti recipe, I would recommend the following sides:\nEveryday Salad \u00a0or\u00a0 Our Family\u2019s Favorite Salad\nRoasted Brussels Sprouts \u00a0or\u00a0 Roasted Asparagus\nBerry Fruit Salad \u00a0or\u00a0 Winter Fruit Salad\nEnjoy, everyone!\nPrint\nChicken Alfredo Baked Ziti\n\u2605 \u2605 \u2605 \u2605 \u2605\n4.9 from 76 reviews\nPrep Time:\n10 minutes\nCook Time:\n30 minutes\nTotal Time:\n40 minutes\nYield:\n0 about 6 - 8 servings 1 x\nPrint\nPin\nDescription\nThis Chicken Alfredo Baked Ziti recipe is made with a lightened-up alfredo sauce, and is always so comforting and delicious.\u00a0 See notes above for possible ingredient variations.\nScale\n1x 2x 3x\nIngredients\nChicken Baked Ziti Ingredients:\n12 ounce s uncooked ziti\u00a0 (or any pasta shape)\n2 cup s shredded, cooked chicken\u00a0 (about 2 small chicken breasts)\n1 batch alfredo sauce\u00a0 (see below)\n1 1/2 cup s shredded part-skim mozzarella cheese\ntoppings: lots of freshly-grated Parmesan cheese, finely-chopped fresh\u00a0basil or parsley\nAlfredo Sauce Ingredients:\n1 tablespoon olive oil or butter\n4 cloves garlic, minced\n3 \u00a0tablespoons all-purpose flour\n1 cup chicken or vegetable stock\n1 cup low-fat milk\n3/4 cup freshly-grated Parmesan cheese\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1/4 teaspoon black pepper\nInstructions\nTo Make The Chicken Baked Ziti:\nPreheat oven to 375\u00b0F.\u00a0 Mist a\u00a0 9 x 13-inch baking dish \u00a0with cooking spray; set aside.\nCook the pasta al dente in a large stockpot of well-salted boiling according to package instructions. Drain. Return pasta to the stockpot and add chicken and alfredo sauce. Gently toss to combine until the pasta is evenly coated.\nPour half of the pasta into the prepared baking dish. Sprinkle evenly with 1 cup of mozzarella. Layer the remaining half of the pasta evenly on top. Sprinkle evenly with the remaining 1/2 cup of mozzarella.\nBake for 20-25 minutes until the cheese is melted and just barely starts to turn golden. Remove and serve immediately, sprinkled with additional toppings if desired.\nTo Make The Alfredo Sauce:\nHeat olive oil in a large sauce\u00a0pan over medium-high heat. Add garlic and saute one minute, stirring occasionally, until fragrant. Sprinkle with flour, and stir to combine. Saute for an additional minute to cook the flour, stirring occasionally.\nSlowly add chicken broth, whisking to combine until smooth. Whisk in milk, and bring the mixture to a simmer. Let cook for an additional minute until thickened, then stir in Parmesan cheese, salt and pepper until the cheese melted. Remove from heat and set aside.\nDid you make this recipe?\nTag @gimmesomeoven on Instagram and hashtag it #gimmesomeoven\nThis post contains affiliate links.\nposted on November 1, 2018 in Entrees / Main Dishes , Pastas\n841 Comments \u00bb\nShare this Post\nYou May Also Like...\nJambalaya\nEasy Cochinita Pibil\nFalafel\nLeave a Reply Cancel reply\nYour email address will not be published. Read my disclosure policy .\nHomemade Alfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese is the creamiest, easiest quick fettuccini Alfredo ever! Made with just 5 ingredients in 20 minutes.\nLearning to cook homemade sauces like\u00a0 Easy Marinara \u00a0makes weeknight cooking so much easier, tastier, and affordable. You won\u2019t have to rely on store-bought sauce when an\u00a0 Italian Food \u00a0craving hits.\nALFREDO SAUCE WITH CREAM CHEESE\nIf you are looking for a quick and easy dinner tonight, this is the Alfredo Sauce for you. Made in less than 20 minutes, this tasty creamy Alfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese tossed with your favorite pastas sure to be a weeknight go-to meal.\nThis Alfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese recipe comes together with just a handful of inexpensive ingredients. It\u2019s much richer and creamier than any store-bought sauce and you can easily double the recipe to freeze for later.\nThis easy creamy sauce can be used in so many ways, not just pasta dishes. Serve Alfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese over wide noodle pastas like fettuccine, cheesy stuffed pastas like tortellini, or substitute it in Meat Lasagna .\nSpoon this creamy sauce over side dishes like Roasted Broccoli and Roasted Red Potatoes to turn them into main dishes. Top Baked Chicken Thighs with this easy Alfredo Sauce for a quick and filling keto dinner.\u00a0\nAlfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese makes an easy and delicious dipping sauce for Garlic Bread or French Roll Breadsticks . Next time you throw a party, keep Alfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese warm in a mini crockpot, stirring occasionally, served with bread for a tasty Italian appetizer.\nMORE EASY, DELICIOUS HOMEMADE SAUCES\nQuick and Easy Marinara Sauce\nHomemade Meat Sauce\nBest Homemade & QUICK Enchilada Sauce (Top 10 Ways to Use It!)\nHomemade Bolognese Sauce\nUsing Grated Parmesan and Cream Cheese:\nThe total time to make Alfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese goes quickly if your cream cheese is softened. Put cream cheese on counter about 30-45 minutes before you want start dinner or just put it in a microwave safe bowl covered with a wet paper towel and microwave it for 90 seconds on half power.\nEither way do NOT use cold cream cheese. If you use cold cream cheese, don\u2019t try to increase the heat to cook faster. Cooking dairy at a high heat curdles it so you won\u2019t get a creamy sauce.\nEasily grate parmesan at home for Alfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese using either the fine side of your cheese grater (making fine shreds) or use a food processor. For this quick and easy version we actually used the grated Parmesan you buy in a shaker and it was DELICIOUS. No gritty aftertaste.\nSave Recipes\nCreate An Account & Save Recipes\nPlease enable JavaScript in your browser to complete this form.\nEmail *\nName\nSign Up Now\nVARIATIONS ON ALFREDO SAUCE WITH CREAM CHEESE\nBacon : Who wouldn\u2019t love Bacon Alfredo Sauce? Cook a few bacon slices until crispy, crumble, and stir into sauce with the parmesan or right before serving.\nVeggies : Add veggies like sun-dried tomatoes, roasted red peppers, fresh diced tomatoes (seeds removed), saut\u00e9ed mushrooms, or thawed frozen peas to your sauce with the parmesan cheese.\nHeavy Cream : For an extra rich and creamy Alfredo Sauce, substitute heavy whipping cream for the whole milk in this recipe. You can also use half and half!\nSpices : Give your Alfredo more flavor with Italian seasoning, red pepper flakes, dried basil, or a pinch of nutmeg. Garnish with fresh chopped Italian parsley.\nCheese : Make this sauce even more creamy and decadent with more fresh shredded cheese like provolone, mozzarella, or white cheddar stirred in at the end until melted.\nFettuccini Alfredo : Toss this creamy sauce with fettuccini pasta cooked to al dente, with a little reserved pasta water as needed, and top with Grilled Chicken Breasts or Grilled Lime Shrimp for an easy dinner.\nEASY ITALIAN PASTA DISHES\nBaked Spaghetti\nBaked Million Dollar Spaghetti\nEasy Bacon Carbonara Pasta\nEasy Skillet Baked Ziti\nHOW TO STORE ALFREDO SAUCE WITH CREAM CHEESE\nServe : This sauce is best served hot and right away but can be at room temperature for up to 2 hours.\nStore : Store Alfredo Sauce in an airtight container in a refrigerator for 3-4 days. Reheat in a medium saucepan over low heat, stirring often.\nFreeze : Cool Alfredo Sauce completely and put in a sealed container, with a small gap between the sauce and the lid. Freeze sauce for 4-6 months and thaw in fridge overnight before reheating.\nPin This\nLike this recipe? Save it to your Pinterest board now!\nPin\nRecipe\nSave\nSave\nPrint\nReview\nAlfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese\nYield:\n8\nPrep Time: 5\nminutes\nCook Time: 15\nminutes\nTotal Time: 20\nminutes\nCourse: Sauce\nCuisine: American, Italian\nAuthor: Sabrina Snyder\nHomemade Alfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese is the creamiest, easiest Alfredo recipe. Toss with any pasta for quick family friendly Italian meal in 20 minutes.\nIngredients\n1/2\ncup\nunsalted butter\n8\nounces\ncream cheese\n, softened\n3\ncloves\ngarlic\n, minced\n1/2\nteaspoon\nkosher salt\n1/4\nteaspoon\ncoarse ground black pepper\n2\ncups\nwhole milk\n2\ncups\ngrated Parmesan cheese\nInstructions\nNote: click on times in the instructions to start a kitchen timer while cooking.\nIn a large dutch oven on medium heat, whisk together the butter, cream cheese, garlic, salt and pepper until smooth and creamy (the cream cheese needs to be softened or this will take a long time).\nSlowly whisk in the milk until smooth.\nWhisk in the grated parmesan cheese and cook for 3-4 minutes until thickened.\nNutrition Information\nYield: 8 , Amount per serving: 345 calories, Calories: 345g, Carbohydrates: 6g, Protein: 13g, Fat: 30g, Saturated Fat: 18g, Cholesterol: 90mg, Sodium: 647mg, Potassium: 155mg, Sugar: 4g, Vitamin A: 1050g, Vitamin C: 1g, Calcium: 379g, Iron: 1g\nAll images and text \u00a9 for Dinner, then Dessert.\nKeyword: Alfredo Sauce with Cream Cheese\nSave\nMade This Recipe?\nShow me what you made on Instagram or Facebook and tag me at @DinnerthenDessert or hashtag it at #dinnerthendessert.\nAbout the Author\nSabrina Snyder\nSabrina is a professionally trained Private Chef of over 10 years with ServSafe Manager certification in food safety.
