All rights reserved.\nTop\n\u2002\u2002\n\u2002\u2002\n"], "_version_": 1665285049545654272, "score": 9.094622}, {"tstamp": ["2020-04-28T09:34:30.711Z"], "digest": ["1ac866c09ab7f890777d78e370ba0f28"], "host": ["thekitchengirl.com"], "boost": [0.3873124], "id": "https://thekitchengirl.com/instant-pot-chicken-alfredo/", "title": ["Instant Pot Chicken Alfredo - The Kitchen Girl"], "url": ["https://thekitchengirl.com/instant-pot-chicken-alfredo/"], "content": ["Instant Pot Chicken Alfredo - The Kitchen Girl\nHOME\nRecipes\nInstant Pot Recipes\nSoup / Stew / Chilis\nMeal Prep Recipes\nGluten-Free Recipes\nAppetizers and Small Bites\nDips Dressings & Sauces\nBreakfast Recipes\nSalad Recipes\nSandwiches and Wraps\nPasta Recipes\nSide Dish Recipes\nSnacks\nSlow Cooker / Crockpot\nMeat and Seafood\nChicken / Poultry\nBeef / Lamb / Pork\nSauces\nOne Pot Recipes\nDessert Recipes\nBeverage / Drink Recipes\nHoliday Recipes\nDairy-Free Recipes\nInstant Pot\n30 Min Meals\nVegetarian\nVegan\nGluten-Free\nMeat Recipes\nChicken / Poultry Recipes\nBeef / Lamb / Pork Recipes\nGlobal Cuisine\nAsian Recipes\nItalian Recipes\nMexican Recipes\nSHOP\nABOUT\nTKG Featured In\nSUBSCRIBE\nPRIVACY POLICY & TERMS OF USE\nHome \u00bb Recipes \u00bb Instant Pot Recipes \u00bb Instant Pot Chicken Alfredo\nInstant Pot Chicken Alfredo\nBy The Kitchen Girl\n39 shares\nInstant Pot Chicken Alfredo is a scrumptious, 30-minute alfredo pasta recipe with tender fettuccini noodles and juicy chicken in a heavenly, white cream sauce.\u00a0This one-pot, toss-and-go recipe is perfect for Instant Pot beginners and busy people. It\u2019s as easy as my Instant Pot Taco Pasta !\nThe Best Chicken Alfredo Pasta\nYou know that dreamy restaurant-style alfredo pasta you crave on the regular and wish you could make at home? Now you can\u2026with minimal effort and a fraction of the cost! The best part, it\u2019s made in your beloved Instant Pot !\nIf you\u2019re a pressure cooker beginner or a very busy person, you\u2019ll have no problem crushing this dump-and-start chicken pasta recipe to get dinner on the table in 30 minutes. It practically makes itself and produces rich, creamy, delicious results every time!\nHow to Make Chicken Alfredo Pasta in the Instant Pot\nBreak uncooked fettucini noodles in half and scatter them in the instant pot in multiple directions. Think of it like a bird\u2019s nest where noodles aren\u2019t resting parallel to each other, but rather stacked in multiple directions.\nScatter butter pieces over the noodles.\nPour in liquids and press pasta noodles under the surface of the liquid.\nPlace uncooked chicken (breast or thighs) on top of the pasta and sprinkle in seasonings. *Note: you can cut the chicken into pieces before pressure cooking or shred it after cooking\u2026your choice. (I prefer to shred it after). See recipe below for details.\nPressure cook for +5 min on high pressure with a 10 min NPR (natural pressure release).\nOpen the lid, transfer chicken to a plate, confirm 165\u00b0 minimum internal temperature, let it rest a minute, and shred it.\nUse tongs to stir the pasta noodles and liquid together.\nAdd parmesan cheese, stirring until sauce thickens.\nAdd shredded chicken to the pasta, serve, and devour.\n* See full recipe below\nGrab my easy Instant Pot recipes\nAlfredo Pasta Instant Pot Cooking tips\nThings to know before you close the Instant Pot lid\nNo pre-cooking : Calling all non -cooks and Instant Pot newbs\u2026this Instant Pot Chicken Alfredo is a dump-and-start recipe. I got you!\nHow to prevent pasta clumping : When adding the uncooked fettuccini noodles to the Instant Pot, break them in half and scatter them in the pot, avoiding stacking them in bundles. Once you\u2019ve added the liquids, don\u2019t stir, just press the noodles down under the liquid surface.\nDo I use raw or cooked chicken for Chicken Alfredo? This Instant Pot chicken recipe was developed using raw chicken. You could use pre-cooked chicken if you like, but you would add it to the alfredo pasta after the cook cycle has completed to prevent drying out.\nChicken breast or chicken thighs : Your choice! Chicken breast is the leaner cut, so it\u2019s quite popular. But chicken thighs seem to never dry out, even as reheated leftovers. Either cut will rock this Instant Pot chicken recipe, but make sure to use the boneless skinless version of either. It\u2019s more convenient than removing bone and skin and reduces the total fat and cholesterol.\nCut up the raw chicken before or after cooking? You are welcome to cut the uncooked chicken breast or thighs into pieces before pressure cooking. However, I prefer to pressure cook them as whole pieces and shred after cooking. This reduces raw-chicken handling, produces fewer dishes, AND helps prevent drying out. FYI, if you go this route, you\u2019ll want to confirm a minimum internal temperature of 165\u00b0 with a meat thermometer at the end of the pressure cooking cycle.\nAfter you open the lid\nIt\u2019s just not very pretty at first : When you first open the lid after pressure cooking Chicken Alfredo, it does NOT resemble a creamy, finished product. Trust me, it\u2019ll get there. First, test your chicken and pasta to make sure they\u2019re adequately cooked before doing the final step that taking this dish to the delicious ending. Here\u2019s how\u2026\nConfirm 165\u00b0 internal temperature of the chicken : If you choose the cook-whole-shred-later option with the chicken in this recipe, you\u2019ll want to confirm a 165\u00b0 minimum internal temperature of the chicken pieces with a meat thermometer after the cook cycle is complete.\nTest the pasta for doneness : Before adding parmesan cheese, test the texture of the pasta noodles to make sure they\u2019re to your liking. They should be fully cooked at this point, as in, slightly beyond al dente. But, if you\u2019re the super -soft pasta type, no prob! Just\u00a0return the lid, close the valve, and add another +1 minute to the instant pot (this time with quick pressure release).\nBringing it all together : Once you\u2019ve confirmed that the pasta and chicken are adequately cooked, it\u2019s time to stir in the parmesan cheese and the sauce will naturally thicken. If you want it thicker, add more parmesan cheese. If you want it thinner, add more liquid.\nNot all pasta brands are equal : I\u2019ve definitely found that different brands of pasta noodles produce different results. This is why I recommend testing the noodles for doneness before thickening the sauce with cheese and pressure cook another minute if needed.\nGrab my easy Instant Pot recipes\nAlfredo Pasta Storage and Reheat tips\nThe pasta soaks up the sauce : When Chicken Alfredo rests after being cooked, it naturally continues to absorb the moisture of the alfredo sauce and can appear dry. I promise you, it\u2019s not dry. It just needs a splash of cream, chicken broth, or plain water during reheat to revive that glistening creaminess that makes alfredo pasta so irresistible.\nFreezing alfredo pasta : I\u2019ve never tried it (because\u2026no leftovers lol), therefore I can\u2019t recommend it based on experience. You\u2019re welcome to try\u2026lemme know if you do!\nChicken Alfredo Ingredient Substitutions\nUse ANY milk in place of half and half (add more parm cheese to balance the fat).\nUse ANY pasta noodles in place of fettuccine.\nUse shredded chicken , canned chicken, or rotisserie chicken instead of raw chicken breast. You\u2019ll add it at the end when you stir in the cheese and allow it to get warm.\nRecommended tools\nInstant Pot\noven mitt (optional to use to open pressure valve)\ntongs\nmeat thermometer\nWant more 30 minute meals?\nInstant Pot Taco Pasta\nBaked Chicken Legs\nLasagna Soup for Instant Pot or Stove\nOrzo Italian Sausage Soup\nInstant Pot Shrimp Pasta in Lemon Cream Sauce\nThai Coconut Soup\nGrab my easy Instant Pot recipes\nPrint REcipe\n5 from 11 votes\nInstant Pot Chicken Alfredo\nInstant Pot Chicken Alfredo is a scrumptious, 30-minute alfredo pasta with tender fettuccini noodles and juicy chicken in a heavenly, white cream sauce.\u00a0It's a simple, dump-and-start Instant Pot recipe, making it perfect for busy people AND pressure cooker beginners.\nPrep Time 5\nmins\nCook Time 25\nmins\nTotal Time 30\nmins\nServings 4\n1-cup servings\nCalories 435 kcal\nAuthor Traci Antonovich from TheKitchenGirl.com\nIngredients\n8\noz\nuncooked Fettuccine Noodles\nbroken in half\n2\nTbsp\nUnsalted Butter\ncubed\n1.5\ncups\nHalf and Half\nor heavy cream\n1\ncup\nWater\nor reduced-sodium chicken broth\n1\n1/2 lb\nuncooked Boneless Skinless Chicken Breast\nor chicken thighs\n1/2\ntsp\nKosher Salt\n1/4\ntsp\nBlack Pepper\n1/2\ncup\nParmesan Reggiano Cheese\ngrated\nInstructions\nHow to Make Chicken Alfredo in the Instant Pot\nBreak the uncooked FETTUCCINI NOODLES in half and scatter them in multiple directions in the Instant Pot. Then scatter BUTTER pieces over the noodles.\n* See note below about scattering noodles to prevent clumping.\nAdd HALF AND HALF and WATER. Don't stir, but DO push the pasta down under the liquid to coat it. Then, make sure it stays under (or very near) the liquid surface.\nLay CHICKEN over the pasta. Sprinkle with SALT and BLACK PEPPER. *See recipe notes below about cooking whole chicken breast or thighs or cutting them first.\nSecure the Instant Pot lid; turn the pressure release valve to the \"Sealing\" position; select \"Manual\" and set the Instant Pot on \"High\" pressure for +5 minutes.\nWhen the cycle completes, allow the Instant Pot to sit for 10 minutes, undisturbed, for a natural pressure release (NPR).\nUse an oven mitt to turn the pressure valve to the \"venting\" position to release any remaining steam. When fully depressurized, press CANCEL on the Instant Pot and open the lid.\nTransfer the chicken to a plate, insert a meat thermometer in the center of the chicken to confirm a minimum internal temperature of 165\u00b0, then allow it to rest for a minute or two. ** See recipe notes below about bringing the chicken up to temperature.\nMeanwhile, stir the pasta and liquid together. Test a few noodles for doneness. If you're happy, go to the next step. ** See recipe notes below about cooking pasta more.\nShred the chicken and add it back to the Instant Pot.\nAdd PARMESAN CHEESE to the pasta, stirring to combine all ingredients. Add more salt and pepper, if needed.\nServing, storage, and reheating instructions\nServe Chicken Alfredo pasta warm garnished with parsley.\nTo store, cool the pasta and refrigerate in an airtight container up to five days.\nTo reheat, add a splash of water, half-and-half, or chicken broth to the pasta before heating it up.\nSERVINGS AND NUTRITION\nYield: 4 cups\nServing size: 1 cup\nNutrition facts are provided as a courtesy and are estimates based on unbranded ingredients acquired from a nutrition database. For accurate calculations, please refer to brand packaging information and consult your nutritionist.\nHow to avoid pasta noodle clumping?\nWhen adding pasta noodles to the cooker, scatter them in multiple directions. Think of it like a bird\u2019s nest where noodles aren\u2019t resting parallel to each other and are touching each other as little as possible.\nDo I cut the chicken (breast or thighs) into pieces\u2026or not?\nYou can pressure cook the chicken without cutting it first, and then shred it after it has cooked. Or you can cut the chicken into bite-sized pieces before pressure cooking. I prefer to leave it intact during cooking, and shred later. This reduces raw-chicken handling, makes fewer dishes, AND helps prevent drying out. Win-win-win!\nIf the chicken didn\u2019t reach 165\u00b0 after the cycle completes\nReturn the chicken piece(s) to the Instant Pot (with the pasta still in it!), close the lid, close the valve seal, and allow the cooker to sit for 5 minutes. Do not program it to cook. You\u2019ll need to depressurize again and remove all steam before opening the lid.\nIf the pasta isn\u2019t soft enough after the cycle completes\nIf you prefer your pasta really soft, close the lid, close the valve seal, and allow the cooker to sit for 5 minutes. Do not program it to cook. You\u2019ll need to depressurize again and remove all steam before opening the lid.\nINGREDIENT SUBSTITUTION IDEAS:\nUse ANY milk in place of half and half (add more parm cheese to balance the fat).\nUse ANY pasta noodles in place of fettuccine.\nUse shredded chicken , canned chicken, or rotisserie chicken instead of raw chicken breast (just add it at the end when you stir in the cheese and allow it to get warm).\nNutrition Facts\nInstant Pot Chicken Alfredo\nAmount Per Serving (1 cup)\nCalories 435\nCalories from Fat 198\n% Daily Value*\nFat 22g 34%\nSaturated Fat 13g 81%\nCholesterol 105mg 35%\nSodium 544mg 24%\nPotassium 268mg 8%\nCarbohydrates 45g 15%\nFiber 2g 8%\nSugar 1g 1%\nProtein 15g 30%\nVitamin A 629IU 13%\nVitamin C 1mg 1%\nCalcium 263mg 26%\nIron 1mg 6%\n* Percent Daily Values are based on a 2000 calorie diet.\nTried this recipe? Mention @thekitchengirl or tag #thekitchengirl\nWhat is Chicken Alfredo?\nChicken Alfredo is a creamy, alfredo pasta dish made with chicken, pasta noodles, and a velvety white cream sauce. It\u2019s a very popular Olive Garden pasta entree that\u2019s very easy to make at home!\nWhat pasta goes with Alfredo sauce?\nYou can use any pasta you like with Alfredo sauce. For this Chicken Alfredo Pasta, we\u2019re using a fettuccine noodle because it\u2019s sturdy and holds up nicely in the Instant Pot.\nWhat should I serve with chicken alfredo?\nServe Chicken Alfredo with a mixed greens Italian salad. Side dish could include broccoli, asparagus, or Brussels sprouts that have been roasted or steamed. Crusty French bread is always a hit with Italian pasta.\nWhat chicken is best for Chicken Alfredo?\nYou can use boneless skinless chicken breast or thighs for chicken alfredo in the Instant Pot. Either one will yield great results, it just depends on which one you prefer. Both will require the same amount of cooking time.\nAuthor\nRecent Posts\nFollow TKG\nThe Kitchen Girl\nRecipe author and food photographer at The Kitchen Girl\nI'm on a mission to help you eat healthy AND save money through simple, everyday recipes, product reviews, and budget-friendly kitchen tips.\nFollow TKG\nLatest posts by The Kitchen Girl ( see all )\nTaco Pasta (Instant Pot or Stove) - 04/22/2020\nFrench Bread Recipe - 04/18/2020\nHow to Cook Dried Beans Without Soaking (in 2 Hours!) - 03/04/2020\n39 shares\n\u00ab Easy Chicken Fried Rice\nEasy Dinner Ideas for Busy Weeknights \u00bb\nJoin TKG's recipe community ... it's FREE!!\nsubscribe\nThank you!\nYou have successfully joined our subscriber list.\nComments\nJB\nsays\n04/27/2020 at 7:52 am\nVery delicious alfredo pasta. All rights reserved.\nHome\nRecipes\nPrev Recipe\nNext Recipe\nChicken Fettuccine Alfredo\nRecipe courtesy of Food Network Kitchen\nRecipe courtesy of Food Network Kitchen\nWatch how to make this recipe.\nChicken Fettuccine Alfredo\nGetting reviews...\nClassic and easy to make, this version of Alfredo doesn't use flour to thicken the sauce. Instead, it relies on a slight simmer and a heavy dose of cheese.\nSave Recipe\nLevel:\nEasy\nTotal:\n25 min\nActive:\n25 min\nYield:\n4 servings\nShare This Recipe\nPinterest\nFacebook\nTwitter\nEmail\nLevel:\nEasy\nTotal:\n25 min\nActive:\n25 min\nYield:\n4 servings\nIngredients\nKosher salt and freshly ground black pepper\n12 ounces fettuccine\nOlive oil, for tossing\n12 ounces boneless, skinless chicken breast (about 2)\u00a0\n1 stick (8 tablespoons) unsalted butter\n2 cups heavy cream\n2 pinches freshly grated nutmeg\n1 1/2 cups freshly grated Parmigiano-Reggiano\u00a0\nDirections\nBring a large pot of water to a boil, and salt generously. Add the pasta and cook according to package directions until al dente, tender but still slightly firm. Strain, and toss with a splash of oil.\nMeanwhile, slice the chicken into 1/4-inch-thick strips, and lay them on a plate or a sheet of waxed paper. Season with salt and pepper.\nHeat a large skillet over medium heat, and add 2 tablespoons of the butter. When the butter melts, raise the heat to medium-high and add the chicken in 1 layer. Cook, without moving the pieces, until the underside has browned, 1 to 2 minutes. Flip the pieces, and cook until browned and fully cooked through, 2 to 3 minutes more. Transfer the chicken to a medium bowl.\nReduce the heat to medium, and add the remaining 6 tablespoons butter. Scrape the bottom of the skillet with a wooden spoon to release any browned bits. When the butter has mostly melted, whisk in the cream and nutmeg and bring to a simmer, then cook for 2 minutes. Lower the heat to keep the sauce just warm.\nWhisk the Parmigiano-Reggiano into the sauce. Add the chicken and cooked pasta, and toss well. Season with salt and pepper. Serve hot in heated bowls.\nCook\u2019s Note\nDon't worry if it seems like there is too much sauce. As soon as everything is tossed together, the sauce will start to cling to the pasta and thicken before your eyes!\nCopyright 2015 Television Food Network, G.P. Please sign in to access your cookbooks Existing members click here to sign in New visitors click here to sign up\nPlease sign in to create shopping lists!\n5 /5 stars\u00a0 \u00a0 100% LIKED IT \u00a0\u00a0\n5 REVIEWS\nALL GOOD\nAdded to 108 cookbooks \u00a0 This recipe has been viewed 46165 times\nA chunky, cheesy delight that is sure to bowl you over! Baked Kidney Beans with Alfredo Sauce features tortillas packed with a fabulously peppy stuffing of kidney beans, chunky veggies and sauces, and laced with creamy Alfredo Sauce. Alfredo Sauce seems similar to continental white sauce, but it has a different texture and even flavour because of the inclusion of cheese. The packed tortillas are placed in a bed of Alfredo Sauce, topped with more sauce and cheese, and baked till it all fuses together into one irresistible treat! Enjoy it right off the oven for the best flavour and texture. Baked Kidney Beans with Alfredo Sauce is a satisfying One Dish Meal , but if you wish you can team it up with with a bowl of Cream Of Carrot Soup and Mexican Fried Rice .\nAdd your private note\nBaked Kidney Beans with Alfredo Sauce recipe - How to make Baked Kidney Beans with Alfredo Sauce\nTags\nItalian Main Dish Casseroles and Bakes One Dish Vegetarian Meals One Meal Dinner Baked Savoury Baked Easy Baked\nPreparation Time:\u00a0 10 mins \u00a0 &nbspCooking Time:\u00a0 20 mins \u00a0 &nbspBaking Time:\u00a0 20 minutes\u00a0 \u00a0Baking Temperature:\u00a0 200\u00b0C (400 \u00b0 F)\u00a0 \u00a0Total Time:\u00a0 50 mins \u00a0 \u00a0 Makes 4 servings\nShow me for\nservings\nIngredients\ntortillas For The Kidney Beans Mixture 1 cup soaked and boiled rajma (kidney beans) 1 1/2 tbsp\noil 1/2 cup\nonion cubes 1/2 cup\ncapsicum cubes (green , yellow , red) 1 tbsp\ndried mixed herbs 1 tsp finely chopped green chillies 1/4 cup\ntomato puree 1 tsp\ntabasco sauce\nsalt and to taste For The Alfredo Sauce 1 tbsp\nbutter 1 tbsp\nplain flour (maida) 1 cup\nmilk 1/4 cup\ngrated processed cheese\nsalt and to taste Other Ingredients 1/4 cup\ngrated processed cheese\nMethod\nFor the kidney beans mixture\nFor the kidney beans mixture\nHeat the oil in a broad non-stick pan, add the onions, capsicums, mixed herbs and green chillies, mix well and saut\u00e9 on medium flame for 3 minutes.\nAdd the tomato pur\u00e9e, \u00bd cup water and salt, cover the pan with a lid and cook on a medium flame for 3 minutes, while stirring occasionally.\nAdd the rajma, tabasco sauce, salt and pepper, mix well and cook on a medium flame for 2 minutes ,while stirring occasionally.\nFor the alfredao sauce\nFor the alfredao sauce\nHeat the butter in a broad non-stick pan, add the plain flour and cook on a medium flame for 30 seconds, while stirring occasionally.\nAdd the milk, mix well and cook on a medium flame for 2 minutes, while stirring occasionally.\nAdd the cheese, salt and pepper and mix well. Keep aside.\nHow to proceed\nHow to proceed\nDivide the kidney beans mixture into 4 equal portions. Keep aside.\nPlace a tortilla on a clean, dry surface, place a portion of the kidney bean mixture at one end, put approx. 2 tsp of alfredo sauce evenly over it and roll it up tightly.\nRepeat step 2 to stuff 3 more tortillas. Keep aside.\nPut \u00bc cup of alfredo sauce in a glass baking dish and spread it evenly, place the 4 stuffed tortillas over it, spread the remaining \u00bc cup of alfredo sauce evenly over it.\nSprinkle cheese on top and bake in a pre-heated oven at 200\u00b0c (400\u00b0f) for 15 minutes.\nServe immediately.\nOther Related Recipes\nNutrient values\u00a0per serving\nEnergy 232 cal Protein 8.2 g Carbohydrates 15.7 g Fiber 1.4 g Fat 14 g Cholesterol 0 mg Vitamin A 383.9 mcg Vitamin B1 0.2 mg Vitamin B2 0.1 mg Vitamin B3 0.3 mg Vitamin C 30.6 mg Folic Acid 9 mcg Calcium 235.3 mg Iron 1.3 mg Magnesium 0 mg Phosphorus 0 mg Sodium 37.5 mg Potassium 99.8 mg Zinc 0.7 mg\nRECIPE SOURCE : Baked Dishes\nAlso View These Related Recipes\nStuffed Baked Beans Bread Tartlets\nBaked Cabbage in Tomato Onion Gravy\nBaked Canneloni with Pomodoro Sauce\nBaked Cheese, Chutney and Mustard Roll\nBaked Corn with Asparagus\nBaked Cr\u00eapes with Capsicum Sauce\nBaked Kidney Beans with Alfredo Sauce\nBaked Mexican Rice with Cheese Patties\nBaked Mushroom Macaroni\nBaked Noodles with Spinach and Yoghurt\nLayered Spinach and Tomato Rice\nBaked Paneer in White Sauce\nReview count\n6 FAVOURABLE REVIEWS\nThe most Helpful Favorable review\n\u00a0Reviewed By \u00a0\n5 of 10 users found this review useful\nSee other 5 star , 4 star , 3 star reviews.\nSee more reviews\nNo review of this type was found\n6 FAVOURABLE REVIEWS\nThe most Helpful Favorable review\n\u00a0Reviewed By \u00a0\n5 of 10 users found this review useful\nSee other 5 star , 4 star , 3 star reviews.\nSee more reviews\nNo review of this type was found\nHelpful reviews for this recipe\nSee all reviews...\nSee all reviews...\nSign in to your account\nRate this recipe\n\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0\nReview this recipe (optional)\nYou are not signed in. The dish was named after Alfredo Di Lelio who opened a restaurant in Rome in 1914 and served \u201cfettuccine all\u2019Alfredo. Fettuccine Alfredo is an exaggerated variation of \"pasta al burro\" or pasta with butter--a dish that Italians understand better as something that would be cooked at home for simplicity and comfort. The dish became popularized in the United States and through commercialization the recipe has evolved to include heavy cream and other ingredients.\nContents\n1\nAlfredo Sauce (original version)\n1.1\nIngredients\n1.2\nPreparation\n2\nAlfredo Sauce (American variation)\n2.1\nIngredients\n2.2\nPreparation\n3\nNotes\nAlfredo Sauce (original version) [ edit ]\nServings: 4 (first course)\nIngredients [ edit ]\n8 oz. or 2 sticks of butter, unsalted and softened to room temperature\n1/2 pound Parmigiano Reggiano cheese (aged 24 months), grated\nSalt\n1 pound Fettuccine egg noodles\nPreparation [ edit ]\nwhisk together the butter and grated Parmesan-Reggiano cheese until it is creamy. Both ingredients combined should be on the thick side.\nPut water to boil in a large pot and prepare the noodles until al dente\nDrain the noodles and reserve 1/2 cup of liquid to emulsify your sauce\nPut noodles back in the warm pot and stir in the butter and cheese mixture with vigorous turning motion while adding pasta water until the noodles are glistening and smooth.\nAdd salt to taste\nServe immediately.\nAlfredo Sauce (American variation) [ edit ]\nThis recipe will make enough sauce for one pound of pasta, which, together, could serve 6 as a first course.\nIngredients [ edit ]\n1\u00be cups (400 ml) heavy cream\n6 tbs. unsalted butter\n8.5 ounces (240 grams) grated Parmesan cheese or asiago cheese\n1 tsp. salt\nfresh-ground black pepper\npinch of fresh-ground nutmeg\nPreparation [ edit ]\nCombine 1\u00bc cups (300 ml) cream and the butter in a pan large enough to accommodate the sauce and later the pound of pasta.\nHeat over a low flame, stirring frequently, until the butter is melted and the cream comes to a bare simmer.\nRemove the pan from the heat once the butter is evenly incorporated into the cream.\nCook the pasta, draining it a little before it reaches the al dente stage. The pasta should be slightly undercooked before being added to the sauce because it will continue to cook while the sauce is being finished.\nDrain the pasta.\nAdd the drained pasta, \u00bd cup (100 ml) of cream, the cheese, the salt, the nutmeg, and several grinds of the pepper mill to the pan\nHeat the pasta and sauce over a low flame, tossing continuously, until the cheese melts into the sauce and the sauce thickens slightly, about one to two minutes. You can add chopped parsley as a garnish mixed into the sauce.\nNotes [ edit ]\nAlfredo Di Lelio, for whom the dish is named, was a Roman innkeeper. Between the 1910s and the 1950s he owned a popular restaurant named Alfredo all'Augusteo in Piazza Augusto Imperatore in the center of the city. The restaurant, now called \"Il Vero Alfredo - Alfredo di Roma\", is run by the granddaughter of Alfredo Di Lelio, Ines Di Lelio.\nThe original name of the dish, created in 1914, was Fettuccine al triplo burro (Fettuccine with triple butter).\nFettuccine is the traditional pasta for Alfredo and its variations because the broad noodles provide just the right platform for the butter fat and cheese.\nFresh egg pasta is greatly preferred by some over dried pasta for cream and cheese sauces because the sauce sometimes clings more readily to fresh pasta than it does to dried.\nWikipedia has related information at Alfredo (sauce)\nRetrieved from \" https://en.wikibooks.org/w/index.php?title=Cookbook:Alfredo_Sauce&oldid=3445254 \"\nCategories :\nEasy recipes\nRecipes\nDairy recipes\nRecipes with metric units\nVegetarian recipes\nNavigation menu\nPersonal tools\nNot logged in\nDiscussion for this IP address\nContributions\nCreate account\nLog in\nNamespaces\nRecipe\nDiscussion\nVariants\nViews\nRead\nEdit\nView history\nMore\nSearch\nNavigation\nMain Page\nHelp\nBrowse\nCookbook\nWikijunior\nFeatured books\nRecent changes\nDonations\nRandom book\nUsing Wikibooks\nCommunity\nReading room\nCommunity portal\nBulletin Board\nHelp out!\nPolicies and guidelines\nContact us\nTools\nWhat links here\nRelated changes\nUpload file\nSpecial pages\nPermanent link\nPage information\nWikidata item\nCite this page\nIn other languages\nAdd links\nSister projects\nWikipedia\nWikiversity\nWiktionary\nWikiquote\nWikisource\nWikinews\nWikivoyage\nCommons\nWikidata\nPrint/export\nCreate a collection\nDownload as PDF\nPrintable version\nThis page was last edited on 22 July 2018, at 02:19.\nText is available under the Creative Commons Attribution-ShareAlike License. ; additional terms may apply. All rights reserved.\nHome\nRecipes\nTrisha Yearwood\nPrev Recipe\nNext Recipe\nWATCH\nWATCH\nLoading Video...\nSee more\n(12)\nChicken Fettuccine Alfredo\nRecipe courtesy of Trisha Yearwood\nRecipe courtesy of Trisha Yearwood\nShow:\nTrisha's Southern Kitchen\nEpisode:\nTrisha's Birthday\nChicken Fettuccine Alfredo\nGetting reviews...\nSave Recipe\nLevel:\nEasy\nTotal:\n30 min\nActive:\n30 min\nYield:\n4 to 6 servings\nShare This Recipe\nPinterest\nFacebook\nTwitter\nEmail\nLevel:\nEasy\nTotal:\n30 min\nActive:\n30 min\nYield:\n4 to 6 servings\nIngredients\n1 pound fettuccine\n1 pound boneless skinless chicken breasts, cut into 1-inch strips\u00a0\nSalt and freshly ground black pepper\u00a0\n1/2 cup all-purpose flour\u00a0\n1/4 cup olive oil\u00a0\n3 tablespoons salted butter\u00a0\n2 cloves garlic, grated\u00a0\n2 cups heavy cream\u00a0\n2 cups grated Parmesan\u00a0\n2 tablespoons finely chopped fresh parsley\u00a0\nDirections\nWATCH\nWatch how to make this recipe.\nBring a large pot of salted water to a boil. Add the pasta and cook according to the package instructions, about 8 minutes. Drain and set aside.\nSeason the chicken with 1 teaspoon salt and some pepper. Dredge in the flour and shake off the excess. Heat the oil and butter in a large saucepan over medium-high heat until the butter melts. Carefully place the dredged chicken into pan. Add the grated garlic. Cook until the chicken is golden brown and cooked through, 4 to 6 minutes. Transfer to a plate and set aside.\nPour the cream into the same pan and bring to a simmer. Stir in the Parmesan. Add the pasta to the mixture and toss to combine. Add the cooked chicken and gently toss. Garnish with the parsley and serve immediately.\nMy Private Notes\nAdd a Note\nWATCH\nShow:\nTrisha's Southern Kitchen\nEpisode:\nTrisha's Birthday\nCategories:\nAlfredo\nChicken Recipes\nPoultry\nMain Dish\nLooking for Something Else?\nQuick & Easy\nMore Chicken Recipes\n5 Ingredients or Less\nHighly Rated\nChicken Fettuccine Alfredo\nChicken and Broccoli Fettuccine Alfredo with Homemade Fettuccine\nShrimp Fettuccine Alfredo\nCajun Chicken Alfredo\nLow-Cal Fettuccine Alfredo\nBow-Tie Skillet Alfredo\nSpring Vegetable Fettuccine Alfredo\nChicken Spaghetti\nGet the Food Network Kitchen App\n\ud83d\udc69\u200d\ud83c\udf73 What's Cooking\nHealthy Dinners \u2014 Fast!\nTop Cauliflower Recipes\n60+ Spring Dinners\nDiscover More Recipes...\nLet's Get Cooking!\nTo sign up, please enable JavaScript.\nSign up for the Recipe of the Day newsletter to receive editor-picked recipes, tips and videos delivered to your inbox daily. All rights reserved.\nPrev Recipe\nNext Recipe\nRecipe courtesy of Food Network Kitchen\nChicken Fettuccine Alfredo\n109\u00a0Reviews\nLevel:\nEasy\nYield:\n4 servings\nTotal:\n25 min\nActive:\n25 min\nAdvertisement\nIngredients\nKosher salt and freshly ground black pepper\n12 ounces fettuccine\nOlive oil, for tossing\n12 ounces boneless, skinless chicken breast (about 2)\u00a0\n1 stick (8 tablespoons) unsalted butter\n2 cups heavy cream\n2 pinches freshly grated nutmeg\n1 1/2 cups freshly grated Parmigiano-Reggiano\u00a0\nDirections\nBring a large pot of water to a boil, and salt generously. Add the pasta and cook according to package directions until al dente, tender but still slightly firm. Strain, and toss with a splash of oil.\nMeanwhile, slice the chicken into 1/4-inch-thick strips, and lay them on a plate or a sheet of waxed paper. Season with salt and pepper.\nHeat a large skillet over medium heat, and add 2 tablespoons of the butter. When the butter melts, raise the heat to medium-high and add the chicken in 1 layer. Cook, without moving the pieces, until the underside has browned, 1 to 2 minutes. Flip the pieces, and cook until browned and fully cooked through, 2 to 3 minutes more. Transfer the chicken to a medium bowl.\nReduce the heat to medium, and add the remaining 6 tablespoons butter. Scrape the bottom of the skillet with a wooden spoon to release any browned bits. When the butter has mostly melted, whisk in the cream and nutmeg and bring to a simmer, then cook for 2 minutes. Lower the heat to keep the sauce just warm.\nWhisk the Parmigiano-Reggiano into the sauce. Add the chicken and cooked pasta, and toss well. Season with salt and pepper. Serve hot in heated bowls.\nCook\u2019s Note\nDon't worry if it seems like there is too much sauce. As soon as everything is tossed together, the sauce will start to cling to the pasta and thicken before your eyes!\nCopyright 2015 Television Food Network, G.P. Add the garlic and lemon zest and cook until the garlic is slightly soft, about 1 minute. Add in the flour and cook, stirring with a wooden spoon,1 minute. Whisk in the milk and 3/4 teaspoon salt and cook, whisking constantly, until just thickened, about 3 minutes. Add the Neufchatel and parmesan cheese; whisk until melted, about 1 minute. Stir in the chopped parsley. Meanwhile, bring a large pot of salted water to a boil. Add the fettuccine and cook until al dente, 2 to 3 minutes. Reserve 1 cup cooking water, then drain the pasta and return to the pot. Add the sauce and 1/2 cup of the reserved cooking water to the pasta and gently toss to combine, adding more cooking water as needed to loosen. Season with salt. Half of the calories and you won\u2019t even be able to tell!\u00a0\nCarbs. Oh man. Carbs are my WEAKNESS. When I am trying to watch what I eat, chocolate and sweets do not tempt me at all. Its the carbs. I dream all day of a big bowl of pasta and carbs sitting right in front of me. Along with a couple of slices of warm bread. I just love my carbs.\nWell stuffing your face with carbs is not the best way of losing weight. And because I count macros, I can only can have 40% in my diet to reach my daily goal. So I decided to take my favorite alfredo sauce and change the ingredients and combine it with whole wheat pasta.\nThis alfredo sauce is the best out there. I changed out some of the ingredients to reduce calories and used low fat milk and reduced fat cream cheese. I was able to cut the calories in half and it was absolutely amazing!\nThis is just one of the recipes that you will want to continue making though out the year. I am such a huge believer in keeping things delicious but swapping out for healthier ingredients to keep your goals throughout the year practical and achievable.\nAnd I still gotta have my carbs. My reward meal each week usually consists of going with the family to the spaghetti factory and loading up on their famous Brown Butter Mazithra Cheese Spaghetti.\nThis is a meal that the entire family is going to love. It comes together easily and is ready to go onto the dinner table in just about 30 minutes!\nWatch a video on how to make Skinny Fettuccini Garlic Alfredo here:\nSkinny Fettuccini Garlic Alfredo\nPrep Time\n15\nminutes\nCook Time\n15\nminutes\nTotal Time\n30\nminutes\nAuthor\nAlyssa Rivers\nServings\n6\nServings\nPrint\nReview\nA lightened up garlic alfredo sauce that is delicious and creamy and coats the pasta perfectly! \u00a0Half of the calories and you won\u2019t even be able to tell!\u00a0\nCourse\nDinner, Main Course\nCuisine\nAmerican, Italian, Italian American\nIngredients\n12\nounce\nwhole wheat fettuchini pasta\nGarlic Alfredo Sauce:\n2\nTablespoons\nButter\n2\ngarlic cloves\nminced\n2\nTablespoons\nflour\n2\ncups\n1% milk\n2\nounces\nReduced Fat Cream Cheese\n1\nteaspoon\ngarlic powder\n1\nteaspoon\nitalian seasoning\n\u00bc\nteaspoon\nsalt\n\u00bc\nteaspoon\npepper\n3/4\ncup\ngrated parmesan cheese\nchopped fresh parsley for garnish\nif desired\nInstructions\nIn a large pot cook the pasta according to package directions. Drain well and set aside.\nIn a large saucepan over medium heat, melt the butter. Add the minced garlics and saute for a couple of minutes until tender. Add the flour and whisk until it is starting to brown. Slowly whisk in the milk and add the cream cheese, garlic powder, italian seasoning, and salt and pepper.\nContinue to whisk until the cream cheese has melted and the sauce is starting to thicken. Add in the grated parmesan cheese and continue to cook for a few minutes.\nStir in pasta and toss to combine. "https://cravinghomecooked.com/easy-pasta-alfredo/", "title": ["Easy Pasta Alfredo - Craving Home Cooked"], "url": ["https://cravinghomecooked.com/easy-pasta-alfredo/"], "content": ["Easy Pasta Alfredo - Craving Home Cooked\nCraving Home Cooked\nDelicious Home Cooked Meals That Everyone Craves\nHome\nRecipes\nCookbook\nBlog\nAbout\nAbout Me\nPrivacy Policy for cravinghomecooked.com\nYou are here: Home\n/\nCourse\n/\nDinner\n/ Easy Pasta Alfredo\nAugust 23, 2018 by Joanna Cismaru | 26 Comments\nEasy Pasta Alfredo\n2.3K shares\nPin 2K\nShare 196\nEmail\nReddit\nYummly 101\nTweet\nJump to Recipe\nPrint Recipe\nEasy Pasta Alfredo \u2013 Creamy, comforting, absolutely delicious, and super easy. This is the best and most simple recipe for Alfredo sauce that you will find!\nThis is one of my absolute favorite sauces to make. Why? Well its incredibly easy , it\u2019s so versatile, and the three main ingredients are butter, cream, and cheese. How can you go wrong with that ?! While I used this sauce over pasta, you can make pizzas and flatbreads with it, or even use it as a dip. Thank you, Italy , for blessing the culinary world once again.\nWhat Is Alfredo Sauce\nNow, some may argue that Alfredo sauce isn\u2019t really Italian- it\u2019s American. I\u2019ll give you a quick history lesson. This sauce was born in Rome from a man named Alfredo. His sauce was a simple emulsification of butter, Parmesan cheese, and pasta. The version we know and love today includes garlic and cream for a saucier consistency. So I guess we can call this modernized sauce an Italian-American lovechild.\nTips for Making the Perfect Alfredo Sauce\nThe sauce will seem thin when you start to mix in the pasta. Don\u2019t worry, just keep tossing. The starches from the pasta will mix into the sauce to give the the perfect consistency. If you use flour or cornstarch to thicken the sauce, it may come out with a gluey consistency once it\u2019s cooled down a bit.\nYou can add a few tsp of Italian seasoning, a pinch of nutmeg or red pepper flakes to add some flare to this sauce. Feel free to get creative with seasoning.\nYou can adjust the ratio of cream to milk in this recipe to suit how rich you\u2019d like it to be.\nIf you try this recipe, please let us know! Leave a comment, rate it and tag a photo #cravinghomecooked on Instagram so we can see it. I always love to see what you guys come up with!\nCraving more delicious recipes?\nSubscribe to my newsletter for FREE and follow along on my Facebook , Pinterest or Instagram page!\n\u00a0\n\u00a0\n\u00a0\nEasy Pasta Alfredo\nEasy Pasta Alfredo - Creamy, comforting, absolutely delicious, and super easy. This is the best and most simple recipe for Alfredo sauce that you will find!\n4.52 from 47 votes\nPrint Recipe\nPin\nRate Recipe\nCourse: Main Course\nCuisine: Italian\nKeyword: cream, parmesan, pasta, pasta alfredo\nPrep Time: 5\nminutes\nCook Time: 10\nminutes\nTotal Time: 15\nminutes\nServings: 4\nCalories: 625 kcal\nAuthor: Joanna Cismaru\nIngredients\n8\noz\npasta , I used linguini\n4\ntbsp\nbutter , unsalted\n2\ncloves\ngarlic , minced\n1 1/2\ncups\nmilk\n1\ncup\nheavy cream\n1/2\ncup\nParmesan cheese , shredded\n1/4\ntsp\nsalt , or to taste\n1/4\ntsp\npepper , or to taste\n2\ntbsp\nfresh parsley , chopped\nUS Customary - Metric\nInstructions\nCook the pasta according to the package instructions.\nMelt the butter in a large skillet over medium high heat. Add the garlic and cook for 30 seconds, or until fragrant.\nPour in the milk and cream. Stir consistently to avoid burning on the bottom of the pan until the mixture comes to a boil. Turn the heat down to medium, and mix in the parmesan cheese, salt, and pepper. Adjust the seasoning to your own taste.\nRemove the pan from the heat and mix in the cooked pasta until the sauce begins to thicken. Garnish with parsley, and serve.\nNotes\nYou can use a larger ratio of milk to cream if you'd like to cut down on calories.\nYou can use any type of pasta that you prefer.\nThis can be served with chicken or mushrooms to add some protein.\nPlease keep in mind that nutritional information is a rough estimate and can vary greatly based on products used.\u00a0\nNutrition\nCalories: 625 kcal | Carbohydrates: 49 g | Protein: 16 g | Fat: 40 g | Saturated Fat: 24 g | Cholesterol: 129 mg | Sodium: 513 mg | Potassium: 313 mg | Fiber: 1 g | Sugar: 6 g | Vitamin A: 1635 IU | Vitamin C: 3.4 mg | Calcium: 311 mg | Iron: 1 mg\ntried this recipe? rate it below! and tag @cravinghomecooked on Instagram and hashtag it #cravinghomecooked !\n2.3K shares\nPin 2K\nShare 196\nEmail\nReddit\nYummly 101\nTweet\n26 Comments\n\u00ab Mojito Recipe\nInstant Pot Mac and Cheese \u00bb\nDisclosure: This post may contain affiliate links. This recipe is for a large dinner party. Please feel free to scale the recipe down for a small family. Note: Make sure you whisk in the flour early while you are melting the butter with the garlic to avoid a &quot;floury&quot; flavor. The flour is important to avoid a thin sauce. This sauce is very versatile. Add grilled marinated chicken for a great Chicken Alfredo. Add saut&eacute;ed shrimp and scallops with Old Bay Seasoning, white wine, shrimp stock, and chopped green onions for Seafood Alfredo. Extra sauce can be frozen for later use.\n34\nPeople talking\nJoin In Now\nJoin the conversation!\nREADY IN:\n45mins\nSERVES:\n14\nYIELD:\n1\ngallon\nUNITS:\nUS\nINGREDIENTS\nNutrition\n2\nquarts heavy cream\n1\nlb butter\n2\ntablespoons flour\n1\nlb freshly grated parmesan cheese\n4\nounces Fontina cheese\n3\ntablespoons minced garlic\n1\nteaspoon salt\n2\nteaspoons black pepper\nNUTRITION INFO\nServing Size: 1 (212) g\nServings Per Recipe: 14\nAMT. PER SERVING\n% DAILY VALUE\nCalories: 880.7\nCalories from Fat 796 g\n90 %\nTotal Fat 88.5 g\n136 %\nSaturated Fat 55.2 g\n275 %\nCholesterol 294 mg\n98 %\nSodium 1010.9 mg\n42 %\nTotal Carbohydrate 6.9 g\n2 %\nDietary Fiber 0.1 g\n0 %\nSugars 0.6 g\n2 %\nProtein 17.9 g\n35 %\nAdvertisement\nDIRECTIONS\nOn medium heat, add butter, garlic, and flour until butter is melted. Do not brown garlic.\nWhisk in the heavy cream until hot.\nSlowly add the freshly grated cheeses into the hot cream mixture. Finally add the salt and pepper. Stir often to make sure no cheese settles at the bottom.\nSimmer until all the cheeses are melted and the sauce reaches the desired thickness. Do not let this sauce boil, or it will begin to separate and the cheeses will become grainy.\nServe with pasta and garnish with freshly grated pecorino romano cheese (used by restaurant), if desired.\nSubmit a Recipe Correction\nAdvertisement\nYOU'LL ALSO LOVE\nBetter Than Olive Garden Alfredo Sauce\nby Parkers Mom\n(607)\nOlive Garden Garlic Alfredo Sauce\nby Diana Adcock\n(227)\nOlive Snacks\nAnnam Kannan\nMy Recipes\nQuick and Easy\nTiffin Receipies\nGo To My CokkBooks\nClose\n21 Apr 2016\nThis recipe has been viewed 46224 times\n5 /5 stars\u00a0 \u00a0 100% LIKED IT \u00a0\u00a0\n5 REVIEWS\nALL GOOD\nA chunky, cheesy delight that is sure to bowl you over! Baked Kidney Beans with Alfredo Sauce features tortillas packed with a fabulously peppy stuffing of kidney beans, chunky veggies and sauces, and laced with creamy Alfredo Sauce. Alfredo Sauce seems similar to continental white sauce, but it has a different texture and even flavour because of the inclusion of cheese. The packed tortillas are placed in a bed of Alfredo Sauce, topped with more sauce and cheese, and baked till it all fuses together into one irresistible treat! Enjoy it right off the oven for the best flavour and texture. Baked Kidney Beans with Alfredo Sauce is a satisfying One Dish Meal , but if you wish you can team it up with with a bowl of Cream Of Carrot Soup and Mexican Fried Rice .\nBaked Kidney Beans with Alfredo Sauce recipe - How to make Baked Kidney Beans with Alfredo Sauce\nTags\nItalian Main Dish Casseroles and Bakes One Dish Vegetarian Meals One Meal Dinner Baked Savoury Baked Easy Baked\nPreparation Time:\u00a0 10 mins \u00a0 &nbspCooking Time:\u00a0 20 mins \u00a0 &nbspBaking Time:\u00a0 20 minutes\u00a0 \u00a0Baking Temperature:\u00a0 200\u00b0C (400 \u00b0 F)\u00a0 \u00a0Total Time:\u00a0 50 mins \u00a0 \u00a0 Makes 4 servings\nShow me for\nservings\nIngredients\ntortillas For The Kidney Beans Mixture 1 cup soaked and boiled rajma (kidney beans) 1 1/2 tbsp\noil 1/2 cup\nonion cubes 1/2 cup\ncapsicum cubes (green , yellow , red) 1 tbsp\ndried mixed herbs 1 tsp finely chopped green chillies 1/4 cup\ntomato puree 1 tsp\ntabasco sauce\nsalt and to taste For The Alfredo Sauce 1 tbsp\nbutter 1 tbsp\nplain flour (maida) 1 cup\nmilk 1/4 cup\ngrated processed cheese\nsalt and to taste Other Ingredients 1/4 cup\ngrated processed cheese\nMethod\nFor the kidney beans mixture\nFor the kidney beans mixture\nHeat the oil in a broad non-stick pan, add the onions, capsicums, mixed herbs and green chillies, mix well and saut\u00e9 on medium flame for 3 minutes.\nAdd the tomato pur\u00e9e, \u00bd cup water and salt, cover the pan with a lid and cook on a medium flame for 3 minutes, while stirring occasionally.\nAdd the rajma, tabasco sauce, salt and pepper, mix well and cook on a medium flame for 2 minutes ,while stirring occasionally.\nFor the alfredao sauce\nFor the alfredao sauce\nHeat the butter in a broad non-stick pan, add the plain flour and cook on a medium flame for 30 seconds, while stirring occasionally.\nAdd the milk, mix well and cook on a medium flame for 2 minutes, while stirring occasionally.\nAdd the cheese, salt and pepper and mix well. Keep aside.\nHow to proceed\nHow to proceed\nDivide the kidney beans mixture into 4 equal portions. Keep aside.\nPlace a tortilla on a clean, dry surface, place a portion of the kidney bean mixture at one end, put approx. 2 tsp of alfredo sauce evenly over it and roll it up tightly.\nRepeat step 2 to stuff 3 more tortillas. Keep aside.\nPut \u00bc cup of alfredo sauce in a glass baking dish and spread it evenly, place the 4 stuffed tortillas over it, spread the remaining \u00bc cup of alfredo sauce evenly over it.\nSprinkle cheese on top and bake in a pre-heated oven at 200\u00b0c (400\u00b0f) for 15 minutes.\nServe immediately.\nNutrient values\u00a0per serving\nEnergy 232 cal Protein 8.2 g Carbohydrates 15.7 g Fiber 1.4 g Fat 14 g Cholesterol 0 mg Vitamin A 383.9 mcg Vitamin B1 0.2 mg Vitamin B2 0.1 mg Vitamin B3 0.3 mg Vitamin C 30.6 mg Folic Acid 9 mcg Calcium 235.3 mg Iron 1.3 mg Magnesium 0 mg Phosphorus 0 mg Sodium 37.5 mg Potassium 99.8 mg Zinc 0.7 mg\nPost A comment\nPost your comment\n5\nPost\nPost your comment\n5\nPost\nReviews\nhttps://www.tarladalal.com/Baked-Kidney-Beans-with-Alfredo-Sauce-31082r Baked Kidney Beans with Alfredo Sauce\nUrvi\n\u00a0on 30 Sep 17 06:08 PM\n5\nVery nicee... worth a try... specially rajma a gud variation\nPost\nCancel\nTarla Dalal\n03 Oct 17 08:32 AM\n\u00a0\u00a0 Hi Urvi, Thank you for your kind words. Add this leftover ham recipe to your holiday collection or make any day of the year. Just like my Chicken Alfredo , this easy pasta recipe satisfies the whole family in under 30 minutes!\nLeftover Ham and Peas Alfredo Pasta Recipe\nDo you need a scrumptious, simple, leftover ham recipe? I got you, friend!\nLast year, I created this entire recipe around a hunk of leftover ham from our holiday dinner with friends.\nGuys, this alfredo pasta is my jam!\nI tossed a few, simple ingredients into one pot and made dinner magic happen.\u00a0Meals using leftovers don\u2019t always go like this.\u00a0But, with this recipe, it\u00a0 totally \u00a0did go like that.\u00a0Talk about a no-fuss dinner!\nThis dish requires a few, quick prep steps, like chopping onion, grating garlic, and dicing ham, then you\u2019re off to the races!\nCan I freeze leftover ham?\nThe answer is yes!\nTo do so, you can seal leftover ham in a freezer bag and store it immediately.\nBe sure to include a package date on your bag, and consume the ham within 6 weeks of that date to avoid freezer burn.\nWhen you pull the ham out of the freezer, go ahead and make my alfredo pasta recipe!\nHow to make ham and peas alfredo pasta in the Instant Pot\nSelect \u201cSaut\u00e9\u201d on the Instant Pot and heat the OLIVE OIL.\nWhen the display reads \u201cHot\u201d, add ONION and GARLIC; saut\u00e9 until tender and fragrant (about 3 min).\nAdd CHICKEN BROTH, PASTA SHELLS, PEAS, HAM, and HALF AND HALF.\nPress the \u201cCancel\u201d function on the Instant Pot. Secure the lid and turn the pressure release valve to the \u201cSealing\u201d position.\nSelect \u201cManual\u201d and set the Instant Pot on \u201cHigh\u201d pressure for +2 minutes for thicker shells like Orecchiette (for thinner pasta shells, reduce time to +1).\nWhen the cycle completes, allow the Instant Pot to sit for 10 minutes, undisturbed, for a natural pressure release (NPR).\nThen, using an oven mitt for protection, release any remaining steam by turning the pressure release valve to the \u201cVenting\u201d position.\nOpen the lid, give the pasta a stir, and fold in PARMESAN CHEESE and BLACK PEPPER to taste. Add SALT if desired.\nThe cooker will stay in \u201cKeep Warm\u201d mode until you shut it off.\n* See full recipe below\nGrab my easy Instant Pot recipes\nHow to make ham and peas alfredo pasta on the stove\nStep 1. \u00a0Saut\u00e9 ONION and GARLIC in olive oil in an 11\u2033 skillet.\nStep 2.\u00a0 Add CHICKEN BROTH and uncooked PASTA; boil until pasta is al dente.\nStep 3.\u00a0 Add PEAS, diced HAM, and HALF AND HALF.\nStep 4.\u00a0 Simmer everything until pasta shells are fully cooked.\nStep 5. \u00a0Stir in parmesan cheese and serve warm.\n* See full recipe below\nI usually make alfredo sauce by itself. But, for this leftover ham recipe, the sauce is made in the same pot with the pasta.\nLeftover Ham and Peas Alfredo Pasta Ingredients\nextra virgin olive oil\nonion\ngarlic\nreduced-sodium chicken broth\nuncooked pasta shells (the thicker the better\u2026I used\u00a0 orecchiette )\nfrozen peas\nleftover ham\nhalf and half (or whole milk)\nparmesan cheese\nblack pepper\nfresh parsley\nRecommended Tools\nchef knife \u00a0and\u00a0 cutting board\nmicroplane fine grater (for cheese)\ngarlic press\n11\u201d stainless skillet\nor 6 qt Instant Pot\nwooden spoon\nOther recipes that use leftover proteins\nLeftover Turkey Shepherd\u2019s Pie\nBlack-Eyed Peas and Ham\nOne-Pot Rotisserie Chicken and Broccoli Rice\nRotisserie Chicken Fried Brown Rice\n40 Leftover Thanksgiving Turkey Recipes\nPrint REcipe\n4.93 from 14 votes\nLeftover Ham Alfredo Pasta Recipe\nLeftover Ham Alfredo Pasta is a one-pot pasta made with cooked ham, peas, pasta shells, and a creamy alfredo sauce. Add this leftover ham recipe to your holiday collection or make any day of the year. This easy alfredo pasta recipe includes Instant Pot and stove cooking methods.\nPrep Time 5\nmins\nCook Time 20\nmins\nTotal Time 25\nmins\nServings 5\n1-cup servings\nCalories 439 kcal\nAuthor Traci Antonovich from TheKitchenGirl.com\nIngredients\n2\nTbsp\nExtra Virgin Olive Oil\n1/4\nlarge\nWhite Onion\ndiced; about 1/2 cup\n3\ncloves\nGarlic\nminced\n3\ncups\nReduced Sodium Chicken Broth\n2\ncups\nUncooked Pasta Shells\nI used Orecchiette\n1\ncup\nFrozen Peas\nthawed\n1\ncup\nHam\ndiced\n2/3\ncup\nHalf and Half\n1\ncup\nParmesan Cheese\n1/2\ntsp\nBlack Pepper\n2\nTbsp\nfresh Parsley\nchopped\nInstructions\nLeftover Ham Alfredo Pasta (Instant Pot)\nSelect \"Saut\u00e9\" on the Instant Pot and heat the OLIVE OIL.\nWhen the display reads \"Hot\", add ONION and GARLIC; saut\u00e9 until tender and fragrant (about 3 min).\nAdd CHICKEN BROTH, PASTA SHELLS, PEAS, HAM, and HALF AND HALF.\nPress the \"Cancel\" function on the Instant Pot. Secure the lid and turn the pressure release valve to the \"Sealing\" position.\nSelect \"Manual\" and set the Instant Pot on \"High\" pressure for +2 minutes for thicker shells like Orecchiette (for thinner pasta shells, reduce time to +1).\nWhen the cycle completes, allow the Instant Pot to sit for 10 minutes, undisturbed, for a natural pressure release (NPR).\nThen, using an oven mitt for protection, release any remaining steam by turning the pressure release valve to the \"Venting\" position.\nOpen the lid, give the pasta a stir, and fold in PARMESAN CHEESE and BLACK PEPPER to taste. Add SALT if desired.\nThe cooker will stay in \"Keep Warm\" mode until you shut it off.\nLeftover Ham Alfredo Pasta (Stove)\nIn an 11\u201d skillet on medium flame, heat EXTRA VIRGIN OLIVE OIL until shimmering (about 2 min).\nAdd ONION and GARLIC; saute until tender and fragrant (about 3 min).\nAdd CHICKEN BROTH and PASTA SHELLS; increase heat to high to reach boiling point.\nReduce heat to medium and cook (uncovered) about 10 minutes; NOTE: pasta will not fully cook during this stage.\nAdd PEAS, HAM, and HALF AND HALF; turn heat to HIGH to bring sauce just to a boil.\nReduce heat to med-low and simmer until pasta shells are cooked to your liking; stirring frequently (3-5 minutes).\nFold in PARMESAN CHEESE, season with BLACK PEPPER. SALT salt if desired.\nServing, Storage, and Reheat Instructions\nServe warm. Garnish with fresh parsley and more parmesan cheese.\nRefrigerate in an airtight container up to 5 days.\nTo reheat, add small amounts of liquid (half-and-half, heavy whipping cream, or milk) before heating via stovetop or microwave. Heat over a medium setting, stirring frequently to avoid overheating/burning.\nSERVINGS AND NUTRITION\nYield: 5 cups\nServing size: 1 cup\nNutrition facts are provided as a courtesy, and are estimates based on unbranded ingredients acquired from a nutrition database. A century along in its development, it's hard to know for sure whether its success was more due to spontaneous reactions from the people who first ate it, or inspired marketing by its inventor.\nThe legend (as seen on the web page of the restaurant owned by the inventor's descendants) goes like this: Once upon a time (all right, 1914), Alfredo di Lelio worked in his parents' little restaurant. He married a lovely girl who eventually became pregnant with their first child: and when she did, she lost her appetite completely. Alfredo was worried about his wife, and tried for a long time to come up with something that would tempt her palate.\nFinally Alfredo made up a batch of a light semolina pasta -- lighter than a plain flour pasta -- and dressed it with nothing but butter and a little Parmigiana-Reggiano cheese. (Here the story as presented on the website takes an inadvertently humorous turn: \"When the dish was ready... he brought it to his wife, saying: \"If you don't want it, I will eat it!!!\" Well, why waste?) Anyway, Mrs. Alfredo (no amount of searching has so far turned up her name -- which just seems wrong, somehow: without her, where would Alfredo's descendants be now?) loved the dish, and gobbled it up.\nAlfredo began offering his new pasta dish in the restaurant, where it became a huge hit. And eventually he went on to open his own restaurant, where famous people from all over the world came to eat his wonderful pasta. The movie stars Douglas Fairbanks and Mary Pickford came too, on their honeymoon, and were so impressed by Alfredo's pasta that they gave him a golden fork and spoon engraved with the words, \"The King of Fettucine.\" And Alfredo became famous all over the world, and lived (we must assume) happily ever after. Certainly his grandson (Alfredo the Third) still presides over the restaurant his father started, and wields the Golden Fork and Spoon with his own hands, and licenses his name all over the place, in distant locales like S\u00e3o Paulo, Mexico City, New York, and Disney World.\nIt's a lovely story. As usual with fairy tales, though, the truth gets somewhat buried under the archetypes. A former correspondent for the New York Times visited Alfredo II's restaurant in the 1950's and reports some unsettling things: that the recipe wasn't original with Alfredo, that it was all over the place under the names fettuccine alla Romana or fettucine alla burro , and that the only thing Alfredo had done differently was to triple the butter. Later it turned out that there were now two sets of the Golden Fork and Spoon, each claiming to be the original. One set can be found at Alfredo's old place at 104 via della Scrofa (sold on when he retired, still operating (though to rather mixed reviews) and actively marketing itself) . The other is at his new place at 30 Piazza Augusto Imperatore (which Alfredo opened at the instigation of businessmen who thought he should market the dish more widely, in conjunction with Italy's Holy Year in 1950). Other food writers suggest that hardly anyone in Italy (except restaurateurs with their eye on the tourist trade) would recognize the dish by the name fettuccine Alfredo or pasta Alfredo . Ordinary Italians generally don't even recognize this simple treatment as a \"dish\", but more the kind of thing that a tired mom would plunk down in front of the kids at the end of the day.\nAt any rate, no culinary legend survives contact with the cooking world for long. The recipe unquestionably became famous: and as soon as that happened, people started messing around with it. It is now hard to find any place serving fettuccine all'Alfredo that does it according to Alfredo I's original recipe -- excepting, of course, his own restaurants. Cream and sometimes even egg yolks have snuck into the recipe somewhere along the line, not to mention peculiar additives like cream cheese, cottage cheese, and other ingredients meant to thicken the sauce less expensively than with that fancy cheese and all that butter. In particular, there are now many people who would not recognize the dish or acknowledge it as fettuccine all'Alfredo if the cream wasn't there. (Ask the manager at Alfredo's of Rome in New York: \"You can tell them five times there's no cream. They won't believe you.\" )\nSo we're offering two versions of the recipe: the original (as revealed by the chef of his New York restaurant) and the simplest version containing cream. Our thought, though, is that the original recipe is probably the best -- and if you make it with good enough pasta, cheese and butter, even the Golden Fork and Spoon probably wouldn't make a difference one way or another.\nClick on \"read more\" for the recipes.\nThe original recipe:\n1 lb. of fresh, thin fettuccine\n6 oz. unsalted butter\n6 oz. Parmigiano Reggiano cheese (aged 24 months), grated\nBring the butter to room temperature. Blend it with the grated cheese in a bowl (or in the small bowl of a food processor if you prefer) until the cheese almost vanishes into the butter: usually this takes two or three minutes. The effect should be that of a smooth, thick cream. Cook the fettuccine noodles in lots of salted boiling water for three minutes. Strain the pasta, leaving it just a little wet, and toss the noodles with the sauce. Serve in pasta bowls. Add some more grated Parmigiano if you like.\nThe version of the recipe that contains cream:\nMMMMM----- Recipe via Meal-Master (tm) v7.01 Title: Fettuccine With Butter & Cream - Fettuccine All'alfredo Categories: Italian, Pasta, Main dish Servings: 6 Basic egg pasta dough * 1/4 c Butter 1 c Whipping cream Salt White pepper 1/4 c Fresh grated Parmesan cheese Additional Parmesan cheese Prepare noodles using Basic Egg Pasta Dough (made with 2-1/4 cup all-purpose flour) Melt butter in a large skillet. When butter foams, add cream. Simmer over medium heat about 2 minutes until slightly thickened. Season with salt and white pepper. Fill a very large saucepan two-thirds full with salted water. Bring water to a boil. Add noodles. Bring water back to a boil and cook noodles uncovered until tender, but firm to bite. Drain noodles and place in skillet with cream. Add 1/4 cup Parmesan cheese. Toss noodles and sauce over medium heat until sauce coats noodles, 20 to 30 seconds. Serve immediately with additional Parmesan cheese. Makes 4 to 6 servings. MMMMM\n\u00a0\nMMMMM----- Recipe via Meal-Master (tm) v8.05 Title: Basic Egg Pasta Dough Categories: Pasta Yield: 8 Servings 4 1/2 c All-purpose flour 6 Eggs Recipe by: Northern Italian Cooking Put flour on a pastry board and make a well in the center. Break the eggs into well; beat with a fork. Draw some flour from inner rim of well over eggs, beating constantly. Keep adding flour a little at a time until you have a soft dough. Put dough aside. With a pastry scraper, remove bits and pieces of dough attached to board. Lightly flour board and your hands. Knead dough 10 to 12 minutes, adding flour a little at a time until dough is smooth and pliable. Insert a finger into center of dough. If it comes out almost dry, dough is ready for pasta machine. If dough is sticky, knead it a little longer adding more flour. Cut an egg-size piece from dough. Wrap remaining dough in a cloth towel to prevent it from drying. Set rollers of pasta machine at their widest setting. Flatten small piece of dough, dust with flour and fold in half. Run it through pasta machine. Repeat this step 5 to 8 times until dough is smooth and not sticky. Change notch of pasta machine to the next setting and run dough through once without folding. Keep changing setting and working pasta sheet through machine until pasta reaches desired thickness. A good thickness for general use is about 1/16 inch. Sprinkle dough with flour between rollings if it is sticky. MMMMM\n\u00a0(By the way, \"fettuccine\" is sometimes spelled \"fettucine\" or \"fettucina\", and the name of the dish is sometimes written\u00a0 \"fettucine Alfredo\" or \"fettucine Alfredo\". Or sometimes even \"fetuccine Alfredo\", or \"fetucini\", or \"fettucini\".)\nTags:\u00a0\nItaly\nItalian\nALfredo\nfettucine\nfettucine alfredo\nfettucine all'Alfredo\nAt our site\nJust viewed\nWhat's hot today\nGermany: Our German Recipe Collection: Meat Recipes\nHow to make (aluminum-free!) baking powder from scratch\nIreland: Wicklow Pancake (March 2, 2007)\nBelgium and the Netherlands: Online Sources for Mayonnaise and Friet Sauces\nIreland: Traditional Irish Soda Bread Without Buttermilk\nItaly: Our Italian Recipe Collection\nIreland: Sausage and Potato Pie\nFront Page\nIreland: Traditional Irish Soda Bread Without Buttermilk\nEuropean Two Letter Country Code Abbreviations\nMalta: \u0126ob\u017c Malti (Maltese Bread)\nPoland: Krem\u00f3wka Papieska / \"Papal\" Cream Cake\nGeneral: What part of the cow does corned beef come from?\nHow to make (aluminum-free!) baking powder from scratch\nPeter's Mum's Soda Bread Recipe\nEngland: Crumpets\nConversion tools\nThis week's featured cookbook\n\u00a0\nLand of Milk and Honey: The Story of Traditional Irish Food And Drink\nBr\u00edd Mahon\nAbout Us\nSince 1995, EuropeanCuisines.com has been the home of an informal collection of European recipes of many kinds, with an emphasis on Irish recipes (since that's where the site runners live). Ready and on the table in less than 20 minutes!\nCrispy golden seared chicken is mixed through a super creamy garlic parmesan Alfredo sauce! Our favourite Chicken Alfredo recipe with the pasta cooked right in is perfect comfort food at its finest.\nCHICKEN ALFREDO\nMove over store-bought Alfredo sauces and even restaurant Alfredo. This chicken Alfredo recipe has the best homemade Alfredo sauce! SO MUCH FLAVOUR!\nThis recipe is for those emergency dinner moments \u2014 a\u00a0 throw-it-all-in-a-pot-recipe you can do in minutes! Just a simple pot and humble stove top needed.\nHOW TO MAKE CHICKEN ALFREDO\nSear chicken thighs (or breasts) first to enjoy the crispy golden texture through the creamy pasta, then remove them to ensure a juicy chicken pieces. You\u2019re more than welcome to dice the chicken first, sear, then leave in the pot to continue cooking with the rest of the ingredients on from Step 2 in the recipe box (at the end of this post).\nTIPS FOR ONE POT ALFREDO\nThere are three main steps to this recipe. CHICKEN \u2192 ALFREDO SAUCE \u2192 PASTA.\nThe sauce I use includes wine. I love wine in this but you can leave it out all together if you wish.\nIf using wine, please use a good quality dry white wine. I use a $20 bottle of Pinot Grigio in most of my recipes on this site, but a good Sav Blanc or Chardonnay will suit the favours in this creamy sauce.\nYou can substitute the heavy cream (or thickened cream) with half and half or a reduced fat cooking cream to reduce the calories. You can also use evaporated milk depending on your dietary requirements.\nUsing freshly grated parmesan cheese enhances the flavour and ensures the cheese melts through the sauce. Please don\u2019t use powdered parmesan.\nRemove the pot off of the stove when the pasta is just cooked al dente (firm to the bite). The sauce begins to evaporate quickly into the hot pasta while it\u2019s resting or waiting to be served.\nChicken Alfredo has never been easier!\nALFREDO SAUCE\nThe sauce in this recipe naturally thickens as the starch from the pasta is released into the sauce while cooking. If the sauce is too thick for your liking, add extra cream (or evaporated milk) in 1/4 cup increments until smooth and silky.\n\u2193\u2193\u2193 LIKE SO\u00a0\u2193\u2193\u2193\nMORE PASTA RECIPES\nSkinny One Pot Chicken Bacon Fettuccine Alfredo\nTuscan Chicken Mac And Cheese (One Pot, Stove Top)\nAvocado Alfredo Zoodles With Chicken + Sun Dried Tomatoes \u00a0(LOW CARB)\nCREAMY CHICKEN ALFREDO RECIPE\nOne Pot Creamy Garlic Parmesan Chicken Alfredo\nCreamy Garlic Parmesan Chicken Alfredo is all cooked in ONE POT! Ready and on the table in less than 20 minutes! Seared chicken is mixed through a super creamy garlic parmesan flavoured pasta with white wine and mushrooms! A favourite Chicken Alfredo recipe!\nPRINT\nSAVE\ngo to your favorites\nPrep: 10\nmins\nCook: 15\nmins\nTotal: 25\nmins\nServes: 4\npeople\nIngredients\n1\nlb\n| 500 g boneless skinless chicken thighs,\n(or breasts)\nSalt and pepper,\nto season\n2\ntbsp\nolive oil,\ndivided\n1\nonion,\ndiced\n4\ncloves\ngarlic,\nminced (or 1 tablespoon minced garlic)\n1/2\ncup\n(125 ml) dry white wine,\n(optional)\n8\noz\n(250 g) brown mushrooms,\nsliced\n2\ncups\n(500 ml) chicken broth,\nor stock\n1 1/2\ncups\n(375 ml) heavy cream, divided\n(thickened cream, light cream, evaporated milk can also be used)\nExtra salt and pepper,\nto taste\n8\noz\n(250 g) dry pasta,\npenne or fettuccini\n1 1/2\ncups\nfreshly grated parmesan cheese\nFresh chopped parsley,\nto garnish\nInstructions\nSeason chicken thighs with salt and pepper.\nHeat half of the oil in a large pot over medium-high heat. Add the chicken thighs and sear on both sides until golden brown and cooked through. Remove chicken and set aside.\nAdd the remaining oil in the pot. Fry onion until transparent, stirring occasionally (about 2 minutes). Saut\u00e9 the garlic until fragrant (30 seconds), then add in the white wine and allow to reduce to half (about 4-5 minutes).\u00a0Add the mushrooms and cook for about a minute, while stirring occasionally.\nPour in broth and 1 cup of cream (or evaporated milk); season with salt and pepper. Bring to a gentle simmer then add the pasta. Mix well, reduce the heat to a slow simmer while stirring occasionally, until pasta is al dente (about 15 minutes).\u00a0\nStir in the parmesan cheese until it melts through the sauce. Remove from heat immediately and slowly add in 1/4-1/2 cup remaining cream if sauce it too thick for your liking. Adjust salt and pepper to your taste.\nSlice the chicken into strips and stir through the pasta. Garnish with fresh parsley and extra parmesan, if desired\nNotes\nYou can dice the chicken first, sear, then leave in the pot to continue cooking with the rest of the ingredients on from Step 2 if you wish.\nUse a good quality dry white wine. Pinot Grigio, Sav Blanc or Chardonnay.\nSubstitute heavy creamy (or thickened cream) with half and half, light cream or evaporated milk.\nIf the sauce is too thick add hot water in 1/4 cup increments until smooth.\nUse freshly grated parmesan cheese.\nRemove the pot off of the stove while there's still a bit of sauce in the bottom of the pot and the pasta is cooked al dente (firm to the bite). The sauce begins to evaporate quite quickly while it sits waiting to be served, and as you mix it through adjusting salt and pepper.\nNutrition\nCalories: 578 kcal | Carbohydrates: 47 g | Protein: 45 g | Fat: 23 g | Saturated Fat: 8 g | Cholesterol: 150 mg | Sodium: 943 mg | Potassium: 804 mg | Fiber: 2 g | Sugar: 6 g | Vitamin A: 410 IU | Vitamin C: 14.3 mg | Calcium: 462 mg | Iron: 2.7 mg\nFiled Under: Chicken\nTagged With: alfredo , alfredo sauce , chicken alfredo , one pot , pasta\nSubscribe to Cafe Delites FOR FREE and Receive Recipes Straight Into Your Inbox!\nE-Mail Address\nPrevious Post: \u00ab MENU PLAN WEEK #13\nNext Post: Garlic Butter Baked Salmon \u00bb\nReader Interactions\nComments\nChris\nsays\nApril 26, 2020 at\nAbsolutely Delicious!! Mattison\nTaste of Home\nCreamy, cheesy and comforting: This easy Alfredo sauce is everything you want in a pasta sauce.\nEvery product is independently selected by our editors. If you buy something through our links, we may earn an affiliate commission.\nGrowing up, pasta was my family\u2019s go-to option for easy weeknight dinners, but we never really made anything from scratch. I know an easy Alfredo sauce only takes a few minutes to pull together, but we were more of a box of pasta, jar of sauce and a vegetable side dish kind of family.\nThen, when I went to culinary school, I learned that a classic Alfredo sauce is nothing more than butter, cream, garlic and Parmesan cheese.\nYou don\u2019t even need the jar of sauce! This Alfredo sauce recipe is simple and creates a creamy, cheesy and super flavorful sauce that comes together in a flash. It almost takes longer to cook the pasta than the sauce. Don\u2019t believe me? Read on to learn how to make Alfredo sauce that\u2019s restaurant-worthy.\nTips on Selecting Ingredients\nAlfredo sauce only contains a handful of ingredients. Everything counts, but the cheese is really the most important factor to making this sauce shine. It\u2019s really important to opt for the highest-quality cheese you can afford.\nIn addition to Parmesan cheese, we added Romano cheese to our recipe. It has a sharp, slightly tangy flavor that adds a level of depth to the sauce. If you just want to use one cheese for simplicity, go ahead and use Parmigiano Reggiano . It\u2019s made in Italy and has a deep, rich, nutty flavor. The cheese labeled \u201cParmesan\u201d isn\u2019t authentic. It might have a similar flavor, but it\u2019s saltier and more acidic than the real deal.\nNo matter what you cheese choose, try to avoid the pre-grated stuff. It doesn\u2019t melt as well, and it may contain anti-clumping agents like plant cellulose.\nWhen it comes to cream, stick with heavy cream. We know\u2014it\u2019s not super healthy\u2014but using it is the only way to get Alfredo sauce to thicken naturally. If you swap in half-and-half or milk, you\u2019ll need to add flour or cornstarch to get it thick enough to coat the noodles.\nEssential Tools You\u2019ll Need\nvia amazon.com\nMicroplane Premium Zester\nvia amazon.com\nGood Grips Flat Wire Whisk\nvia amazon.com\nAll-Clad Stainless Cookware\nA multi-clad 12-inch stainless steel fry pan\n($130) is our go-to piece of cookware for making pasta sauces. It\u2019s the perfect size for tossing cooked pasta with sauce. If you need, you can also use it to simmer the noodles in the sauce for an extra boost of thickening power. As a bonus, it\u2019s also oven-safe, so you could use it to make baked pasta, too.\nYou\u2019ll also want a flat wire whisk ($8) when making cream sauces. It\u2019s important to stir constantly when adding the cream (and again when adding the cheese) to keep the sauce from breaking. Broken sauce is greasy and unpalatable, but it\u2019s easy to avoid with the right tools.\nWe also recommend using a Microplane\n($14) for grating the cheese. You could use any old box grater, but the Microplane creates super fine shreds of cheese that melt seamlessly into the sauce. It\u2019s not just good for cheese, either; use it to zest citrus fruit, grate chocolate or create ground nutmeg.\nEasy Alfredo Sauce Recipe\nTaste of Home\nIngredients\n4 ounces uncooked fettuccine\n3 tablespoons butter\n1 garlic clove, minced\n1 cup heavy whipping cream\n1/4 cup plus 2 tablespoons grated Parmigiano Reggiano cheese, divided\n1/4 cup grated Romano cheese\n1/8 teaspoon salt\nDash ground black pepper\nDash ground nutmeg\nMinced fresh parsley, optional\nYield : 2 servings\nInstructions\nStep 1: Cook the pasta\nCook the fettuccine in seasoned pasta water according to the directions for al dente. When it\u2019s finished, drain but don\u2019t rinse it. You don\u2019t want to remove the starch that coats the outside of the noodles, which helps the sauce stick to the pasta. If the pasta finishes before the sauce, you can toss it with a little bit of olive oil or butter to keep the noodles from sticking together.\nStep 2: Prepare the sauce\nIn a large saute pan, melt the butter over medium heat. Add the minced garlic and cook until it\u2019s fragrant, about 1 minute. Then, slowly add the heavy cream, whisking constantly as you pour until all the cream is incorporated. Bring the mixture up to a gentle simmer and let it cook for 3 to 4 minutes, until it begins to thicken.\nEditor\u2019s Tip : You can use a saucepan to make the sauce, but we like using a 12-inch fry pan instead. It\u2019s large enough to make the sauce and toss the pasta, so you don\u2019t have to dirty any extra dishes.\nStep 3: Add the cheese\nRemove the pan from the heat. Add a handful of the Parmesan and Romano cheese at a time, whisking to incorporate the first handful before adding the next. When all the cheese is added, return the pan to the stovetop. Simmer the sauce gently over low heat for 3 to 4 minutes, until it\u2019s thick enough to coat the back of a spoon.\nEditor\u2019s Tip : Be careful not to boil the sauce at this point. If the heat is too high, the sauce will break and separate.\nStep 4: Season and serve\nSeason the sauce with salt, black pepper and nutmeg. Add the drained fettuccine to the pan and toss it with the sauce. Portion the pasta into individual bowls and top them with the remaining Parmesan cheese and parsley, if using.\nHow to Thicken Alfredo Sauce\nIf you make the recipe with heavy cream, you shouldn\u2019t need to thicken this Alfredo sauce. Heavy cream contains at least 36% butterfat (as compared to milk\u2019s 3.5% and half-and-half\u2019s 12%). When the cream comes to a simmer, the water content evaporates, leaving a deliciously thick sauce behind. The cheese also adds body when it melts, giving you a naturally thick sauce.\nEveryone\u2019s preferences are different, so you may prefer a sauce that\u2019s thicker than the recipe below. You have a few options for\u00a0 thickening sauce without using flour or cornstarch:\nSimmer the pasta in the sauce . The pasta will exude extra starch, adding body to the sauce.\nAdd extra cheese . It will only make the sauce cheesier and more delicious, so go for it!\nAdd an ounce or two of cream cheese . Cream cheese is naturally thick and creamy, and it has the right flavor profile for Alfredo, too.\nTry an egg yolk . Eggs are great for thickening sauces, but they can scramble when exposed to hot temperatures. You\u2019ll need to temper the yolk first by whisking a cup of the hot sauce into a bowl with the yolk. Then, you can add the tempered yolk mixture to the pot.\nHow to Make a Healthy Alfredo Sauce\nFor a lighter version of Alfredo sauce, try making a roux with one tablespoon each butter and flour. After about two minutes, when the mixture is foamy and bubbling, add your liquid of choice to create a white sauce . You can use one cup of regular milk, half-and-half or a mixture of chicken stock and heavy cream.\nFor a gluten-free version, feel free to use 1-1/2 teaspoons of cornstarch instead. Create a slurry by mixing it with a tablespoon or two of water. Then, bring the liquid to a simmer and whisk in the slurry. Continue to simmer until the mixture is thickened.\nTips for Storage\nProperly stored, cooked pasta can last three to five days in the refrigerator. That said, pasta isn\u2019t the ideal candidate for leftovers. The noodles will continue to absorb moisture as it sits in the refrigerator, so it will be simultaneously soggy and dry upon reheating. We\u2019ve had the best luck by storing pasta in an airtight container and reheating it with an extra splash of milk. It\u2019s not as good as the first day, but it won\u2019t be dry!\nAdd a teaspoon or two of milk or water to the leftover pasta and cook it over low heat on the stovetop. You can also use the microwave at 50% power. Take care not to heat the pasta too quickly, or the sauce will separate and become greasy. Check out these other ways to reheat pasta .\nWhat to Make with Alfredo Sauce\nOnce you\u2019ve mastered this easy Alfredo sauce recipe, use it to make any number of delicious pasta dishes. It\u2019s great with chicken and shrimp (especially when they\u2019re seasoned with Cajun seasoning ). You can also add any number of vegetables, like spinach or kale, broccoli, spring peas, asparagus, mushrooms, zucchini and more.\u00a0Check out these recipes that start with Alfredo sauce .\n1 / 20\nTaste of Home\nGarden Vegetable Gnocchi\nWhen we go meatless, we toss gnocchi (my husband's favorite) with veggies and a dab of pesto. I use zucchini in this, too. \u2014Elisabeth Larsen, Pleasant Grove, Utah\nGet Recipe\nTaste of Home\nHam Ravioli Bake\nI based this recipe on a dish my husband likes to order when we go out for Italian food. All rights reserved.\nPrev Recipe\nNext Recipe\nRecipe courtesy of Food Network Kitchen\nShrimp Fettuccine Alfredo\n65\u00a0Reviews\nLevel:\nEasy\nYield:\n4 servings\nTotal:\n25 min\nActive:\n25 min\nAdvertisement\nIngredients\nKosher salt\n12 ounces fettuccine\nOlive oil, for tossing\n3/4 pound large shrimp (about 16), peeled and deveined, tails removed\nFreshly ground black pepper\n1 stick (8 tablespoons) unsalted butter\n2 cups heavy cream\n2 pinches freshly grated nutmeg\n1 1/2 cups freshly grated Parmigiano-Reggiano cheese\nDirections\nBring a large pot of water to a boil, and salt generously. Add the pasta, and boil according to package directions until al dente, tender but still slightly firm. Strain, and toss with a splash of oil.\nMeanwhile, arrange the shrimp in a single layer on a large pie pan or paper plate, and pat them with a paper towel until completely dry. Season with salt and pepper.\nHeat a large skillet over medium heat, and add 2 tablespoons of the butter. When the butter melts, raise the heat to medium-high, and invert the plate of shrimp over the skillet so the shrimp fall into the pan all at once. Cook the shrimp, without moving them, until the underside is pink, 1 to 2 minutes. Flip the shrimp, and cook until fully pink and cooked through, about 2 minutes more. Transfer the shrimp to a bowl.\nReduce the heat to medium, and add the remaining 6 tablespoons butter. Scrape the bottom of the skillet with a wooden spoon to release any browned bits. When the butter has mostly melted, whisk in the cream and nutmeg and bring to a simmer, then cook for 2 minutes. Lower the heat to keep the sauce warm.\nWhisk the Parmigiano-Reggiano into the sauce. Add the shrimp and cooked pasta, and toss well. Season with salt and pepper. Serve hot in heated bowls.\nCook\u2019s Note\nDon't worry if it seems like there is too much sauce. As soon as everything is tossed together, the sauce will start to cling to the pasta and thicken before your eyes.\nCopyright 2015 Television Food Network, G.P. Slightly reducing the cream and adding a hefty dose of cheese means you don't have to use flour to thicken the sauce.\nSave Recipe\nLevel:\nEasy\nTotal:\n25 min\nActive:\n25 min\nYield:\n4 servings\nShare This Recipe\nPinterest\nFacebook\nTwitter\nEmail\nLevel:\nEasy\nTotal:\n25 min\nActive:\n25 min\nYield:\n4 servings\nIngredients\nKosher salt\n12 ounces fettuccine\nOlive oil, for tossing\n3/4 pound large shrimp (about 16), peeled and deveined, tails removed\nFreshly ground black pepper\n1 stick (8 tablespoons) unsalted butter\n2 cups heavy cream\n2 pinches freshly grated nutmeg\n1 1/2 cups freshly grated Parmigiano-Reggiano cheese\nDirections\nBring a large pot of water to a boil, and salt generously.
